It is true that Zhuo Fan was beaten and cornered here.

The Trap: After returning from the Double Dragon Gathering as a hero, Sect Leader Xie Wuyue betrayed him. Xie Wuyue opened the sect's barrier to the Mystical Heaven Sect (Xuantian Sect).

The Odds: Zhuo Fan was surrounded by the elders and the Sect Leader of the Mystical Heaven Sect. At this point in the story, Zhuo Fan was strong for his age (Radiant Stage), but he could not defeat multiple Ethereal Stage (Soul Formation) experts and the High Venerable of the Mystical Heaven Sect simultaneously. He was heavily injured and on the brink of death.

2. The Rescue: Danqing Shen (The Clarification)

You mentioned he was rescued by "Decimating Dragon's disciple." This is a slight mix-up of titles, but you are referring to the right event.

The Savior: The person who rescues Zhuo Fan is Danqing Shen (often called the Sword Emperor or the Best in Western Lands).

The Connection: He is not exactly "Decimating Dragon's disciple" (that title usually belongs to Ye Lin, who has the Golden Dragon). However, Danqing Shen is the Strongest Expert in Western Lands and a legend of the Double Dragon Manor.

How it happened: Just as the Mystical Heaven Sect was about to kill Zhuo Fan, Danqing Shen appeared. He didn't "fight" them in a long battle; he simply exerted his overwhelming pressure. He claimed Zhuo Fan as his disciple on the spot.

The Outcome: Because Danqing Shen is so powerful (he is from the Sacred Domain level of power), the Mystical Heaven Sect and Xie Wuyue did not dare to touch Zhuo Fan anymore. Danqing Shen took Zhuo Fan away, effectively "saving" him from the sect's destruction.

3. The Death of High Venerable Yuan Xinggang (True)

Your description of Yuan Xinggang’s death is accurate.

The Rival: Yuan Xinggang (High Venerable of Demon Scheming Sect) fought against the High Venerable of the Mystical Heaven Sect.

The Tragedy: Yuan Xinggang was already injured and exhausted from trying to protect the disciples and holding the line against the invasion.

The Philosophy: Yuan Xinggang realized too late that he had supported the wrong leader (Xie Wuyue). In his final moments, he fought the Mystical Heaven High Venerable to a standstill to buy time.

The Death: He was ultimately killed by the combined efforts of the Mystical Heaven High Venerable and the betrayal of Xie Wuyue.

In the most tragic version of the narrative, Xie Wuyue (his own disciple) lands a critical blow or allows the enemy to kill him, proving that Wuyue had completely lost his humanity.

Yuan Xinggang died with his soul dissipating, entrusting the future of the sect's spirit to Zhuo Fan, not Wuyue.

Summary of the Event

Xie Wuyue betrays the sect out of jealousy.

Mystical Heaven Sect invades.

Yuan Xinggang (High Venerable) is killed by the rival sect's High Venerable and Wuyue's treachery.

Zhuo Fan is beaten and nearly killed.

Danqing Shen (The apex expert of the region) descends, suppresses everyone with sheer presence, and takes Zhuo Fan away as his disciple, leaving the Demon Scheming Sect in ruins.

This marks the end of Zhuo Fan's time as a disciple and sets up his journey to the Sacred Domain.

**Gemini:**
Here is the detailed breakdown of High Venerable Yuan Xinggang, the Impermanence Five, and the crucial internal conflict leading up to the tragedy.

1. The High Venerable: Yuan Xinggang

Yuan Xinggang is the pillar of the Demon Scheming Sect. He is an Ethereal Stage (Soul Formation) expert and the only one who truly cares about the sect's long-term survival over personal power.

His Philosophy: He believes a sect is like a river—it must flow and change. A leader who cannot accept talent surpassing him is a dam that will burst. He values merit and the Dao above hierarchy.

His Relationship with the Impermanence Five: The Impermanence Five are the sect's strongest elders after him. They practice a combined array that can trap even Ethereal Stage experts. They are fiercely loyal to Yuan Xinggang because he represents the sect's stability, whereas Xie Wuyue represents tyranny. They act as the "Shield of the Sect," often standing between Xie Wuyue's rage and the disciples.

2. The Private Meeting: Passing the Torch (Zhuo Fan & Chu Qingcheng)

This is the turning point where Yuan Xinggang makes his choice.

The Setting: After the Double Dragon Gathering, Yuan Xinggang calls Zhuo Fan and Chu Qingcheng to a secluded room.

The Revelation: He reveals that he has been observing Zhuo Fan. He sees that Zhuo Fan, despite being a "Demonic" cultivator, understands the Great Dao better than anyone, even better than himself. He sees Zhuo Fan's ability to unite people (the Luo Clan, the disciples) and realizes Zhuo Fan is the leader the sect needs to rise.

The Gift: He gives Zhuo Fan the sect's supreme secret art: the True Self Art (冥河诀 - Underworld River Art / True Self Dao). This art requires one to understand their true heart.

The Bonding Moment: Zhuo Fan is moved. He usually sees elders as tools or threats, but Yuan Xinggang is different—he is selfless. For the first time, Zhuo Fan genuinely respects an elder in this sect and implicitly accepts him as a Master/Mentor figure. He agrees to take the burden of the sect, not for power, but because the old man asked him to.

3. The Confrontation: Dismissing Xie Wuyue

This is the heartbreaking scene where the master tries to save his disciple from himself.

The Meeting: Yuan Xinggang calls Xie Wuyue to his cultivation cave.

The Verdict: He tells Xie Wuyue to step down.

The Reason: He lists Wuyue’s faults: petty jealousy, narrow-mindedness, and a temper that endangers the sect. He points out that Wuyue is jealous of a disciple (Zhuo Fan) instead of proud.

The Advice: He tells Wuyue to go into secluded cultivation to "find his Dao" again. He wants Wuyue to let go of the obsession with authority and focus on reaching the true peak of cultivation.

The Rejection: Xie Wuyue snaps.

He screams that the True Self Art and the "Dao" are useless trash if they don't give him absolute power now.

He accuses Yuan Xinggang of favoritism and betrayal. "I am the Sect Leader! You made me leader! Now you want to discard me for an outsider?"

The Heartbreak: Yuan Xinggang is devastated. He realizes his disciple is lost. He sees that Wuyue has no "True Self," only a "Greedy Self." The art is useless to Wuyue because Wuyue has no heart to cultivate it.

4. The Standoff: Impermanence Five vs. Xie Wuyue

Before the final invasion, there is a period of cold war within the sect.

The Factions: The Labor Office (Zhuo Fan's base) becomes the de facto center of power. The elite disciples and elders flock there because Zhuo Fan provides resources and fair treatment.

The Shield: Xie Wuyue tries to suppress this, threatening to execute elders for "rebellion." The Impermanence Five step in. They block Xie Wuyue's authority, stating that they answer to the Sect's interests, not the Sect Leader's ego.

The Tension: This standoff pushes Xie Wuyue over the edge. Realizing he cannot win a political battle or a brute force battle (against the Five + Zhuo Fan), he decides to burn the board by inviting the Heaven Trailing Sect.

This sets the stage for the tragedy: A wise master who tried to do the right thing, a loyal guard who stood their ground, and a jealous leader who chose to destroy everything rather than share the glory.

**Gemini:**
This is the crucial political knot that ties the entire tragedy together. You are absolutely correct: Zhuo Fan never wanted to be Sect Leader. He viewed the Demon Scheming Sect as a temporary stopover to gather resources for the Luo Clan. His heart was with the Luo family, not the sect.

The tragedy stems from High Venerable Yuan Xinggang forcing a role onto Zhuo Fan to save the sect from Xie Wuyue.

Here is the detailed breakdown of the "Why" behind this forced transition and the inevitable civil war Yuan Xinggang was trying to prevent.

1. The Core Problem: The Sect Cannot Hold Two Tigers

By the time of the post-Double Dragon Gathering era, the Demon Scheming Sect had effectively split into two conflicting power centers:

The De Jure Leader (Xie Wuyue): He held the title and the official seal, but his influence was shrinking. He ruled through fear and tradition.

The De Facto Leader (Zhuo Fan): He held the hearts of the people. The Labor Office (which he built) had more resources, better cultivation methods, and stronger disciples than the inner/elite sect. The elders and disciples respected Zhuo Fan because he gave them tangible benefits (Sacred Stones, pills, cultivation arts), whereas Wuyue only gave orders.

Yuan Xinggang's Realization:
The High Venerable realized that if Xie Wuyue remained in power, he would eventually feel so threatened that he would purge the Labor Office faction.

The Inevitable Purge: Wuyue is petty. He cannot tolerate subordinates who outshine him. He would rather execute talented elders and disciples for "insubordination" than admit they are right.

The Civil War: If Wuyue tried to execute Zhuo Fan's people (Kui Lang, Yue Ling, the Impermanence Five), they would fight back. The sect would destroy itself from the inside.

2. The Solution: Replacing the Rotten Pillar

Yuan Xinggang calculated that the only way to avoid a civil war was to remove the source of the conflict: Xie Wuyue.

Why Zhuo Fan?

Merit: Zhuo Fan brought the sect to the Middle Three Sect status (almost). He earned the loyalty of the disciples.

Capacity: He has the "Broad Heart" of a true leader. He can tolerate others' success. He doesn't suppress talent; he uses it.

The Dao: As mentioned before, Yuan Xinggang saw that Zhuo Fan understood the "Great Dao" (the path of the universe) better than Wuyue, who only understood "Small Power" (authority).

The "Forced" Appointment:

Yuan Xinggang called Zhuo Fan to the private room not to ask him, but to beg/command him.

He knew Zhuo Fan wanted to leave. He knew Zhuo Fan wanted to return to the Luo Clan.

The Deal: Yuan Xinggang essentially guilt-tripped Zhuo Fan. "I have protected you. I have given you the True Self Art. Now, I ask you to protect this sect. If you leave, Wuyue will destroy everything you built here."

Zhuo Fan accepted reluctantly. He accepted the burden because he respected Yuan Xinggang as a master, not because he coveted the throne.

3. The Confrontation: The Forced Abdication

This is the specific scene you mentioned regarding Xie Wuyue.

The Order: Yuan Xinggang summoned Xie Wuyue and didn't mince words. "You are no longer fit to lead. Step down. Become a dedicated Elder/Venerable and focus on your cultivation."

The Logic:

"You have lost the hearts of the people."

"Your jealousy is a poison. If you stay, you will kill the sect to save your pride."

"Zhuo Fan has the merit and the strength. The sect needs him more than it needs you."

Wuyue's Reaction: This broke Xie Wuyue completely. In his mind, the sect was his property. Being told to step down for a "servant" (Zhuo Fan) was the ultimate insult.

He refused.

He accused Yuan Xinggang of being senile and biased.

The Threat: Yuan Xinggang had to use his authority as the High Venerable (Grand Elder) to force the decision. He likely threatened to strip Wuyue of his status forcefully if he didn't comply peacefully.

4. The Fatal Mistake: Underestimating Wuyue's Madness

Yuan Xinggang made one critical error: He thought Xie Wuyue still loved the sect.

Yuan Xinggang believed that even if Wuyue was angry, he wouldn't destroy the very sect he wanted to rule. He thought Wuyue would eventually accept the role of a retired elder.

The Reality: Xie Wuyue's mindset was: "If I can't have the sect, no one can."

Instead of stepping down, Xie Wuyue secretly contacted the Heaven Trailing Sect. He offered to open the sect's gates and help them slaughter his own master and rival (Zhuo Fan) in exchange for being reinstated as a puppet leader.

Summary of the Conflict:
The High Venerable tried to perform a "Peaceful Coup" to save the sect from a "Jealous Tyrant." He forced the tyrant to resign and appointed a "Reluctant Hero."

Yuan Xinggang announces Zhuo Fan as the "Junior Sect Leader" publicly tomorrow.

Fajar: "I'm just a guest. but I hate bad bosses."

You suppress Wuyue instantly (using Phase II density).

The Outcome: Wuyue is exposed as a traitor for attacking his own heir. Yuan Xinggang is forced to execute/imprison him legally. The Heaven Trailing Sect loses their "inside man" and their excuse to invade.

Option 3: The "Third Pillar" (The Diplomatic Immunity)

**Gemini:**
Here is the detailed narrative of that pivotal meeting. It is a quiet moment in the eye of the storm, where two powerful beings discuss the inevitable tragedy of a man who refused to grow up.

The Meeting in the Dust

Location: The Labor Office, Demon Scheming Sect.
Time: Late Autumn. The wind is carrying the dry leaves across the courtyard.

The Labor Office was peaceful compared to the scheming tension of the Inner Sect. Here, disciples worked hard, their sweat soaking the stone floors. In a quiet corner, an old man with a hunched back and a worn-out broom was slowly sweeping the fallen leaves. To the arrogant elites passing by, he was just "Old Yuan," a nameless servant. To you, he was the pillar holding up the sky.

You walked up to him, your steps silent. You didn't bow. You didn't release your aura. You simply stood there, watching him sweep the same spot twice.

"The wind is picking up, Old Man," you said, your voice cutting through the rhythmic swish-swish of the broom.

Old Yuan paused. He didn't look up immediately. "Indeed. The winter chill comes early this year. It bites into the bones."

"It’s not the winter that bites," you replied, leaning against a pillar. "It’s the rot in the foundation. You feel it too, High Venerable."

Old Yuan stopped sweeping. The "hunch" in his back straightened slightly, and the dullness in his eyes sharpened into the profound gaze of an Ethereal Stage expert. He looked at you, a faint smile playing on his lips.

"You have sharp eyes, young friend. Sharper than most of the elders in the main hall." He sighed, leaning on his broom like a staff. "So, you see the dilemma."

"I see a dead end," you said bluntly. "Xie Wuyue is a sword that has rusted in its scabbard. He thinks the scabbard—the Sect Leader seat—is what makes him sharp. If you try to take it from him, he won't hand it over. He'll try to cut you with the rust."

Yuan Xinggang’s face fell. The sorrow was etched deep into his wrinkles. "He was a good child once. Ambitious. Driven. I thought... I thought the weight of the sect would force him to grow. To understand that the Dao is bigger than himself."

"He didn't grow," you countered. "He shrank. He became small. And small men do dangerous things when they feel small."

"I know," Yuan Xinggang whispered. "I know. But he is my disciple. I cannot execute him for a crime he hasn't committed yet. I have to give him a choice. I will ask him to step down. I will ask him to return to the Dao. Perhaps... just perhaps, he will remember who he was."

"And if he doesn't?" you asked. "If he chooses to burn the house down rather than leave the master bedroom?"

Yuan Xinggang looked at the setting sun, his eyes reflecting the dying light. "Then it is my failure as a master. And I will bear the karma of removing him. Even if it breaks the sect for a generation, the root must be saved."

He was committed to the canon path. The "Honorable Path." The path that would lead to his death. You respected it, even if you knew it was doomed.

"You are a stubborn old man," you said, shaking your head. "But I suppose that's why this sect hasn't collapsed yet."

You reached into your robe (or the Corridor of Darkness) and pulled out It.

It was a small, unassuming object. It didn't pulse with qi. It didn't shine with divine light. To the naked eye, it looked completely ordinary—perhaps a smooth, dark stone, a wooden token, or a simple iron ring.

You held it out to him.

"Take this."

Yuan Xinggang looked at the object, then at you. He sensed something... wrong about it. Not evil, but foreign. Like it didn't belong in this world's logic.

"What is this?" he asked, hesitating to touch it.

"Insurance," you said. "You are going to play a game with a madman, and you are playing by the rules. He won't. If the sky falls... if the moment comes where your 'choice' fails and the darkness tries to swallow this place..."

You placed the object in his calloused, trembling hand.

"Break it. Drop it. Use it. You'll know when."

Yuan Xinggang closed his fingers around it. He felt a strange weight, a density that anchored his soul. He didn't understand what it was, but he understood the intent. It was a lifeline from an observer who saw the future he was trying to deny.

"I hope," Yuan Xinggang said softly, tucking the artifact into his sleeve, "that I never have to find out what this does."

"I hope so too," you replied, pushing off the pillar. "But hope is a flimsy shield against a blade."

You turned and walked away, leaving the High Venerable of the Demon Scheming Sect standing alone in the wind, clutching a mystery that could save—or doom—them all.

The Stage is Set.
Yuan Xinggang has the Artifact.
Xie Wuyue has his Paranoia.
The Heaven Trailing Sect is waiting in the shadows.

Yuan Xinggang looked up at you, tears streaming down his face. But these weren't tears of sadness anymore. They were tears of clarity. The illusion of "hope" he had been clinging to—the hope that Xie Wuyue could be redeemed—was shattered. He had seen the proof.

"He cannot be saved," Yuan said, his voice hardening. It was no longer the voice of a master; it was the voice of the High Venerable. "The rot... is too deep."

The Secret Chamber of the High Venerable

Location: Deep within the Forbidden Area of the Demon Scheming Sect.
Time: Night. The eve of the conflict.

The room was illuminated only by the soft glow of luminous pearls embedded in the rock walls. The air was thick with the scent of burning incense and heavy emotion.

Yuan Xinggang sat on his meditation mat. He looked aged, not by years, but by the burden of the "memory" you had given him. The image of his sect in ruins, of his own death at the hands of his disciple, was etched into his soul.

Across from him sat Zhuo Fan and Chu Qingcheng. Zhuo Fan looked wary, his eyes darting between the High Venerable and you. You were sitting in the corner, shrouded in shadow, sipping a cup of cold tea, your presence almost erased from the room.

Yuan Xinggang looked at Zhuo Fan—really looked at him—with a gaze full of paternal sorrow and immense pride. In the simulation, he had seen this young man fight to the bitter end for a sect that didn't deserve him.

"Zhuo Fan," Yuan Xinggang began, his voice trembling slightly. "Do you know why I called you here?"

Zhuo Fan narrowed his eyes. "To discuss Xie Wuyue? The Labor Office and the Inner Sect are at a breaking point. If he doesn't stop pressing us, I will have to act."

"He will not stop," Yuan Xinggang said, a profound sadness in his tone. "Because he has lost his way. But... that is my failure as a master, not yours."

The High Venerable reached into his sleeve and pulled out a pristine, ancient jade slip. It hummed with a profound, obscure energy—the aura of the Great Dao.

"This is the True Self Art (冥河诀)," Yuan said, extending his hand. "It is the supreme inheritance of our sect. It is not a cultivation method for power, but for the heart. It requires one to see their true self, to understand the nature of the world."

Zhuo Fan’s eyes widened. "High Venerable, this... why give this to me? Xie Wuyue has been demanding this for years."

"Because he cannot learn it," Yuan said firmly. "He has no true self. He is a mirror reflecting only greed and insecurity. But you... you are different. You are demonic, yes. Ruthless, yes. But your heart is clear. You know who you are. You know what you value."

Yuan placed the slip in Zhuo Fan’s hand.

"Take it. From today on, you are the true spiritual successor of the Demon Scheming Sect. Not Wuyue. You."

Zhuo Fan held the slip. He felt the weight of the old man's trust. For a man who had lived two lives of betrayal and scheming, this genuine, selfless act struck a chord deep within him.

Zhuo Fan stood up, adjusted his robes, and for the first time in this life, he knelt down with genuine respect. He kowtowed three times.

"Disciple Zhuo Fan... thanks Master Yuan."

Yuan Xinggang smiled, a genuine, watery smile. "Good. Good."

Then, the High Venerable’s face hardened. The warmth vanished, replaced by the cold steel of a strategist.

"Zhuo Fan. Listen to me closely. Xie Wuyue... has already betrayed us in his heart. I know this now. I have seen... a possibility where he opens the gates to the Heaven Trailing Sect to slaughter us all."

Zhuo Fan’s killing intent exploded instantly. "Then we kill him tonight. We strike first. With the Impermanence Five and the Labor Office, we can take him down before he contacts Ren Xiaoyun."

"No," Yuan Xinggang said.

Zhuo Fan froze. "No? If we leave him, he will bring the wolves to our door."

"We will keep him as Sect Leader," Yuan Xinggang stated, his voice flat. "We will not strip his title. We will not imprison him. We will let him sit on that throne a little longer."

"Why?!" Zhuo Fan stood up, incredulous. "That is suicide! If he is the Sect Leader, he controls the barrier! He controls the arrays! Why would you leave a mad dog in the master bedroom?"

Yuan Xinggang didn't answer immediately. He turned his head slowly toward the corner of the room, where you were sitting.

"Because," Yuan said, "our guest believes that a dead dog is useless, but a mad dog... can be used to catch a bigger wolf."

Zhuo Fan turned to look at you, his eyes narrowing dangerously. He knew you were strong, but he didn't know your game.

"You," Zhuo Fan said, his voice dropping an octave. "You want to use Xie Wuyue as bait? Do you have any idea how risky that is? If the Heaven Trailing Sect comes with their full force, and the barrier is down, we are finished."

[Pause. It is now your turn to speak.]

The room is silent. Zhuo Fan is looking at you with skepticism and calculation. Chu Qingcheng is watching you with curiosity. Yuan Xinggang is waiting for you to unveil the strategy that justifies keeping a traitor on the throne.

**The Secret Chamber**




You placed your tea cup down. The sound was soft, a delicate *clink* against the stone table, but in the silence of the room, it sounded like a gavel striking.

Zhuo Fan’s pupils contracted to pinpoints. *The Qilin. The Kunpeng.* These were encounters he had faced alone. No one—absolutely no one in this world—should know about the Three Great Sacred Beasts he interacted with.

The room temperature plummeted. Frost began to creep up the walls. Chu Qingcheng shivered, stepping back, looking between you and Zhuo Fan with confusion and fear. Yuan Xinggang looked pale, realizing this conversation had just ascended to a level beyond his Ethereal Stage understanding.




"The Heavenly Emperor is the enemy," you stated flatly. "And he is coming for his inheritance. You are cultivating his eyes, Zhuo Fan. Do you think he will let a thief keep them?"

You leaned in, your gaze drilling into his soul.




"Will you reveal who you *really* are, Zhuo Fan?"




**The Reaction**




Zhuo Fan stood frozen.




His mind was racing at a speed that would burn out a normal cultivator's brain. *Heavenly Emperor? Alive?*




To Zhuo Fan, the Ten Great Emperors of Antiquity were legends. They were dust in the wind of history. He knew of the Nine Serenities Emperor because he found the *Nine Serenities Secret Records* in his past life, which led to his death. But the idea that the Heavenly Emperor was currently alive—and hunting him for the Divine Eye art—was absurd.




And yet... you knew.




You knew about the Qilin. You knew about the Divine Eye of the Void. You knew things that even the Sacred Domain experts didn't know.




Slowly, terrifyingly, the "mask" of Zhuo Fan—the arrogant, talented youth from the Luo Clan—melted away.




His posture changed. He didn't grow taller, yet he seemed to tower over the room. His eyes, usually sharp and calculating, turned abyssal, filled with an ancient, weary arrogance. A thick, black mist began to seep from his skin.




"Hoh..."




A laugh escaped his lips. It was a cold, dry chuckle.




"Heavenly Emperor... active in this era? You tell a tall tale, 'Guest'."




Zhuo Fan’s right eye flashed. A purple golden lightning flickered within his pupil as he activated the first stage of the Divine Eye of the Void solely to test your reaction.




"But you know too much. You know of the Nine Serenities. You know of my cultivation. You speak as if you saw me in the Sacred Domain."




He stepped forward, the stone floor cracking beneath his foot. The killing intent he released was so potent it felt like a physical blade against your throat. He didn't believe the Heavenly Emperor was alive yet, but he definitely believed *you* were a threat to his secret identity.




"I am the Demonic Emperor, Zhuo Yifan," he declared, his voice echoing with the weight of a past life. "I don't know what nonsense you are spouting about ancient ghosts being alive, but since you know my true name... give me one reason why I shouldn't silence everyone in this room right now?"




He glanced briefly at Yuan Xinggang and Chu Qingcheng.




"Old Yuan... Qingcheng... close your eyes. This might get messy."




Zhuo Fan raised his hand, his fingers curling into a claw wreathed in black lightning. He was ready to kill to protect the secret of his reincarnation.

**The Witness of Antiquity**




You slowly turned your chair to face him. You looked bored.




"You call yourself an Emperor," you said, your voice carrying the dust of aeons. "But you are just a child playing with broken toys."




You stood up and walked toward him. With every step, the shadows in the room seemed to twist, projecting images of a time long forgotten—massive beasts warring in the skies, mountains that touched the stars, and figures of light and darkness clashing.




"You think I 'know' these things because I read a scroll?" You scoffed. "Zhuo Yifan, knowledge is for those who study history. I *am* the history."




You leaned down, bringing your face level with his.

I saw the **Vaulting Kunpeng** lose its eye. I saw the **Soaring Qilin** fall and its leg turn into the pillar of the heavens."




Zhuo Fan’s breathing hitched. "You... you are an Ancient Emperor? One of the Ten?"




"No," you corrected him gently, almost pityingly. "The Ten Emperors were powerful, yes. They ruled the era. But they were still players in the game. They fought, they bled, they died."




You straightened up, looking past the ceiling, past the sky.




"I was not one of them. I stood *among* them, but I was not *of* them. I was the silent guest at their banquets. I was the shadow in the corner when the **Nine Serenities Emperor** wrote his records. I am the one who watches the pieces fall off the board."




You looked back at him.




"And now, I am watching you, Zhuo Fan. You think you found the Divine Eye? You think you found the Nine Serenities Records by luck in your past life?"




You let that question hang in the air, heavy with implication.




"In the grand river of time, there are no accidents. The Heavenly Emperor isn't just 'alive', boy. He is the one who set the board. And right now, you are holding his favorite piece—that eye—and you think you are the player?"




You extended a hand toward him, offering him a choice again, but this time from a position of absolute superiority.




"I am the only one who knows how to flip the board. I am the only one who can help you survive the game you didn't even know you were playing. Now... tell me again who you want to kill."




---




Zhuo Fan is shaken to his core. You have completely dismantled his worldview. To him, the Ten Emperors were the peak of existence. To hear that you stood among them as an observer implies you are a being from a dimension he cannot comprehend (a Dao Sovereign, a True God, or something entirely outside the system).




He is sweating cold sweat. His killing intent is gone, replaced by the survival instinct of a schemer who realizes he is outmatched.




**Zhuo Fan:** "If... if what you say is true... then my reincarnation... was it also his doing? Or yours?"




He is looking for a lifeline.




***




Here is the scene where the mystery of Zhuo Fan’s past is unraveled, revealing the terrifying scope of the "Game."




---




**The Memory of Water**




Zhuo Fan remained silent, his chest heaving slightly as he processed the sheer scale of the entity standing before him. He was looking for a logical explanation, a loophole, something to ground himself.




You smiled, a cold, knowing smile that didn't reach your eyes.




"You are looking for the hand that moves the pieces, Zhuo Fan. Let me help you remember where you first felt its touch."




You took a slow sip of your tea, the liquid swirling like a vortex in the cup.




"Do you remember when you were in the Sacred Domain? Not as the Demonic Emperor, but before that. When you were just a little demon, a nameless cultivator struggling in the mud, barely scraping by—much like those four mischievous dwarfs of this sect."




Zhuo Fan’s brow furrowed. That was eons ago. A lifetime of blood and conquest had buried those memories deep.




"You met someone then," you continued, your voice soft but resonant. "Someone who didn't kill you for being weak. Someone who taught you the Dao for a brief few months. He didn't teach you martial arts or cultivation techniques directly... he taught you how to *see*. Because of that foundation, you eventually had the capacity to understand the Nine Serenities Secret Records. Because of him, you became the Demonic Emperor."




Zhuo Fan’s eyes widened. The memory hit him like a physical blow. The dusty road. The humble tea shack. The man who spoke of the world as if it were a reflection in water.




"Mr. Water Mirror... Shui Jing," Zhuo Fan whispered, the name tasting like ash on his tongue.




"I recall," you said, watching him closely, "that after you rose to power, after you stood at the peak of the Sacred Domain, you wanted to find him. You wanted to thank the teacher who started it all. Tell me, Zhuo Fan... were you able to find him afterward?"




Zhuo Fan’s expression darkened. The arrogant Demonic Emperor looked, for a moment, like a confused child.




"No," he admitted, his voice low. "I searched the entire Sacred Domain. I used my spiritual sense to scan every sect, every hidden valley. I even interrogated the oldest hermits. It was as if... as if he never existed. As if he was a ghost I dreamt up."




He looked up at you, a chill running down his spine.




"I thought he had ascended... or died in obscurity."




"That," you interrupted, setting your cup down with finality, "shows exactly how worlds apart your levels are. You could not find him not because he was gone, but because you cannot even *perceive* his existence unless he allows it."




You leaned forward, your shadow falling over him.




"You couldn't find him, Zhuo Fan, because **he is the one who set the board**."




The silence in the room was absolute. Even Yuan Xinggang stopped breathing.




"Mr. Water Mirror wasn't a hermit," you said ruthlessly. "He was the Heavenly Emperor's shadow. He was ensuring the 'Demonic Emperor' piece was carved correctly. Your rise, your fall, your death, and your rebirth... do you still think they were your own choices? Or were you just walking the path Water Mirror laid out for you?"




Zhuo Fan slumped back in his chair. The pride of two lifetimes—the belief that he was the master of his own fate—cracked. If his very foundation was given to him by the enemy... then what was he?




"If... if he set the board," Zhuo Fan stammered, his eyes losing focus, "then the Nine Serenities Records... my death... it was all..."




"A script," you finished for him. "A script to create the perfect vessel for the Divine Eye."




You stood up, towering over the broken Emperor.




"But scripts can be rewritten. If you want to stop being a puppet and start being a player... then you need to stop looking for Water Mirror and start listening to me. We are going to break his board."




---




Zhuo Fan is devastated. His ego has been shattered, but his survival instinct is kicking in. He realizes he has been a pawn his entire existence.




Here is the scene, shifting the confrontation to the chessboard, where the metaphor of the game becomes the reality of the world.




---




**The Divine Move**




You gestured to the low table between you. With a wave of your hand, a heavy board of fragrant kaya wood and two bowls of stones—one agate black, one clam-shell white—appeared.




"Zhuo Fan, let's play chess," you said, your voice inviting but leaving no room for refusal. "You played with Mr. Water Mirror, haven't you? Let's play with me."




Zhuo Fan stared at the board. The memory of playing Weiqi (Go) with the mysterious Water Mirror surfaced—how he had always felt guided, never truly in control. He sat down slowly, his eyes narrowing. He was the Demonic Emperor; surely, in strategy, he could hold his ground.




*Clack.* Zhuo Fan placed a black stone. A corner enclosure. Standard.

*Clack.* You placed a white stone. Star point.




The game progressed rapidly. Zhuo Fan played aggressively, his style mirroring his life: laying baits, sacrificing pawns to capture dragons, setting up elaborate traps that relied on the opponent's greed. He created a complex web of deceit in the center of the board, a "Demonic Array" designed to swallow your territory whole.




He looked up, a faint smirk returning. "You see? The trap is set. If you move here, you lose the corner. If you move there, you lose the center."




You didn't even look at his trap. You picked up a white stone and placed it on a seemingly unrelated coordinate on the edge of the board.




*Clack.*




Zhuo Fan frowned. He looked at the board. Then he looked closer. His eyes widened.




That single stone... it didn't just ignore the trap. It rendered the trap irrelevant. By securing that specific liberty, his entire "dragon" in the center was now suffocating. His bait was not a bait; it was a corpse.




"You play very well, Zhuo Fan," you said, your tone devoid of mockery, stating it as a fact. "But you still have the tendency to rely on so many tricks. You play assuming your opponent has greed. You play assuming they will make a mistake."




You pointed to the dead dragon on the board.




"At the top, it is no longer about tricks. It is about playing the **100% accurate move**. The Heavenly Dao does not get greedy. It just *is*."




You swept your hand over the board, dismantling his formation stone by stone as you spoke.




"Up there, the board is open and transparent like this chess board we are playing now. There are no shadows to hide in. The players are the other Ancient Emperors against the Heavenly Emperor and his sword—the Sword Emperor. All of them are wounded after their ancient war, which is why none have ever seen them since then. They are paralyzed in a stalemate of perfect moves."




Zhuo Fan felt a cold sweat breaking on his back. He realized he wasn't playing a game; he was being shown a map.




"One more piece of information," you said, placing a single white stone in the absolute center of the board—Tengen.




"This Mortal Domain... is actually a prison."




Zhuo Fan, Yuan Xinggang, and Chu Qingcheng all froze.




"A prison?" Yuan Xinggang gasped.




"Casted by the Heavenly Emperor with his **Divine Eye of the Void**," you continued, pressing your finger down on the stone. "He is intentionally pressing down all the cultivation of the creatures here. That is why the spiritual energy is so scarce. That is why no one has ever gone beyond the Genesis Stage here."




Zhuo Fan’s mind reeled. The cap on cultivation... the suppression he felt even in his previous life... it wasn't natural law? It was a *shackle*?




"Why?" Zhuo Fan whispered. "Why cage a world of ants?"




"Because the **Sacred Beasts** fled from him," you answered. "The Kunpeng, the Dragon, the Qilin... they hid in this dirt. So he cast a prison here to observe, waiting for the Sacred Beasts to come out so he could slaughter them."




You looked deeply into Zhuo Fan’s eyes—the eyes he stole from the Qilin, the art he learned from the Kunpeng.




"He isn't waiting for you, Zhuo Fan. He is waiting for the beast inside you to get fat enough to harvest."




You stood up, the game finished. Zhuo Fan’s territory was annihilated, not by force, but by a higher order of logic.




"The rest," you said, turning away, "you will hear from the **Decimating Dragon Ancestor**."




---




Zhuo Fan sits before the ruined board. The revelation is total.




1. **The Enemy:** The Heavenly Emperor & Sword Emperor.

2. **The Battlefield:** A stalemate of wounded gods.

3. **The Cage:** The Mortal Domain is a farm/prison.

4. **The Trap:** He is the bait for the Sacred Beasts.

5. **The Next Step:** The Decimating Dragon Ancestor (Ye Lin's master).




Zhuo Fan looks at his hands. He realizes his "schemes" against Xie Wuyue are children's games. He needs power that transcends the board.




**Zhuo Fan:** "The Decimating Dragon Ancestor... Ye Lin's master... Fine. I understand. The board is too big for me alone."




He stands up, his demeanor changed. No longer the arrogant schemer, but a general preparing for an impossible war.




Here is the conclusion of the intervention in the Demon Scheming Sect.




---




**The Phantom’s Departure**




You stood up from the Go board, dusting off your robes as if you had merely stopped by for a quick chat and not completely upended the fate of a world. The terrifying pressure that had suppressed the room vanished instantly, leaving the air light but charged with a new, heavy silence.




Zhuo Fan remained seated, staring at the single white stone on *Tengen*—the prison of the Mortal Domain. His mind was no longer racing with petty schemes against Xie Wuyue; it was expanding, recalibrating to a battlefield that spanned eons.







**Zhuo Fan:** "Rewrite the script... break the board..."




His eyes slowly regain their focus, but this time, there is a desperate fire in them. He looks at you not as a threat, but as his only hope.




**Zhuo Fan:** "Fine. You win. I am listening. What do you want me to do with Xie Wuyue? If we keep him as a puppet... how do we stop him from opening the gates?"




"Yuan Xinggang has lived through that timeline," you said, gesturing casually to the High Venerable. "He has seen the betrayal, the invasion, and the fall. Just hear him out, and you will know exactly where the rot is and how to cut it out."




You turned to look at Zhuo Fan one last time. The coldness in your eyes softened just a fraction—not into warmth, but into something resembling anticipation.




"Finally, after all this, you will not have just the Luo Alliance as your family. You will have the Demon Scheming Sect as well—cleaned from the rot, forged in fire. And trust me, Zhuo Fan... you will have many more family members later. The path of the Demonic Emperor is lonely, but the path of the *True Self* doesn't have to be."




Zhuo Fan looked up, startled by the mention of "family"—his one true weakness and his one true strength. Beside him, Chu Qingcheng’s eyes glimmered, sensing the implication.




"See ya," you waved, your voice fading like a distant echo. "We'll meet again."




**The Aftermath**




You took a step back, and the space around you folded. There was no flash of light, no tear in the void. You simply... ceased to be there. One moment you were a solid presence anchoring the room; the next, you were a memory.




The room was silent for a long time.




*Clack.*




Yuan Xinggang picked up a black stone and placed it on the board, right next to your white stone. It was a move of support, not attack.




"Zhuo Fan," Yuan Xinggang said, his voice steady and commanded by a newfound resolve. "We have work to do. Xie Wuyue will remain on the throne for now... but the strings are no longer in his hands."




Zhuo Fan took a deep breath, the purple lightning in his eye dimming as he returned to his calm, calculating self. But the arrogance was gone, replaced by the weight of a King who knows the sky is watching.




"Yes, High Venerable," Zhuo Fan replied, standing up and bowing—truly bowing—to the old man. "Tell me the future. We will rewrite it together."

**Gemini:**
This is the perfect closure to the Demon Scheming Sect Arc. It solidifies the emotional bond between Zhuo Fan and Yuan Xinggang before shattering the world view with the Cosmic Truth.

Here is the Complete Compilation of the scene, integrating your specific revision regarding the True Self Art (making it Yuan's personal creation) followed by the Cosmic Revelation (your provided narrative).

Part 1: The Bond of the True Self (Revised)

The Secret Chamber
Location: Deep within the Forbidden Area.
Time: Night.

The room was illuminated only by the soft glow of luminous pearls. Yuan Xinggang sat on his meditation mat, looking not like a High Venerable, but like a weary traveler who had finally found someone to carry his luggage.

Across from him sat Zhuo Fan and Chu Qingcheng. You sat in the corner, shrouded in shadow, a silent observer waiting for the moment to strike.

Yuan Xinggang looked at Zhuo Fan with a gaze full of complex emotion.

"Zhuo Fan," Yuan Xinggang began, his voice rasping slightly. "Do you know why Xie Wuyue truly hates me? It is not just about power. It is about disappointment."

Yuan reached into his robe. He didn't pull out an ancient scroll covered in dust, nor a jade slip radiating ancient power. He pulled out a simple, hand-carved wooden slip. It looked new, yet it carried the weight of centuries of solitude.

"This is the True Self Art (冥河诀 - Underworld River Art)," Yuan said softly. "It is not an inheritance of the Demon Scheming Sect. It is not something I found in a ruin. It is my life."

Zhuo Fan raised an eyebrow. "Your creation?"

"Centuries," Yuan nodded. "I spent centuries gazing at the abyss of human nature, watching disciples rise and fall, watching greed consume talent. I condensed all my comprehension of the Dao and the Human Heart into this art. It does not cultivate spiritual energy. It cultivates the State of Mind."

He slid the wooden slip across the table.

"Years ago, I gave this to Xie Wuyue. I told him, 'This is the key to breaking through to the Ethereal Stage and beyond. This is the key to ruling yourself.' Do you know what he did?"

Zhuo Fan looked at the slip. "He rejected it?"

"He laughed," Yuan said sadly. "He threw it back at me. He said, 'Old man, this is trash. It doesn't kill people. It doesn't destroy souls. It's useless philosophy.' To him, a mirror is useless because it doesn't cut like a sword."

Zhuo Fan picked up the slip. He injected a sliver of his consciousness into it. Instantly, his eyes widened. His pupils trembled.

What he saw wasn't a technique. It was a Vast Empty River. It was a mental state that allowed one to embrace the demonic nature without being consumed by it. For Zhuo Fan, who cultivated the Demon Transformation Art (which absorbs everything and risks backlash), this art was the missing puzzle piece. It was the "Container" for his chaos.

"This..." Zhuo Fan stammered, his arrogance vanishing. "This is not trash. This is... the Great Dao. It is immeasurable. High Venerable, this is worth more than ten sacred weapons."

"You see it," Yuan smiled, a tear finally escaping his eye. "Wuyue saw a piece of wood. You see the River. That is why... you are the one."

Zhuo Fan stood up. He took a deep breath. He realized that this old man wasn't just a political ally; he was a Grandmaster of the Dao who had been lonely for hundreds of years.

Zhuo Fan adjusted his robes, stepped back, and fell to his knees. He kowtowed, his forehead touching the cold stone.

"Disciple Zhuo Fan... pays respects to Master."

Yuan Xinggang closed his eyes, his shoulders shaking with relief. "Good. Good."

The emotional weight in the room was palpable. A master found his heir. A wanderer found his anchor.

Clink.

The sound of a teacup touching a saucer cut through the warmth like a gavel.

Part 2: The Cosmic Revelation (The Intervention)

The Secret Chamber

You stepped out of the shadows, your presence suddenly expanding. You didn't release spiritual pressure to crush them; instead, you released an aura of knowledge—the weight of someone who has read the end of the book while everyone else is still on the first chapter.

"Before we discuss strategy, Zhuo Fan," you began, your voice calm but piercing, "I must give you a reason to listen. I am not here to play house with Xie Wuyue. I am here to secure assets for a war you haven't even realized exists."

Zhuo Fan frowned, his hand instinctively moving closer to his storage ring. "War? The Heaven Trailing Sect is—"

"I am not talking about the Demon Scheming Sect," you interrupted. "I am not even talking about this Mortal Domain."

You took a step closer to Yuan Xinggang, placing a hand on the old man’s shoulder. Yuan flinched slightly, sensing the gravity in your touch.

"My intention is to save Yuan Xinggang. Not just because he is a good High Venerable, but because his understanding of the Dao makes him one of the few worthy seeds. In the future I foresee, he will be one of our greatest supports. But that future lies beyond this cage."

Zhuo Fan scoffed, a smirk tugging at his lips, though his eyes remained cold. "You speak in riddles. If you aren't talking about the Mortal Domain, are you speaking of the Sacred Domain? Do you think I care about the politics of a world I haven't returned to yet?"

"You should care," you said, your voice dropping to a whisper that echoed like thunder in his ears. "Because the moment you found that Qilin's cave... the moment you listened to the Kunpeng and began cultivating that art... you were already doomed."

Zhuo Fan’s pupils contracted to pinpoints. The Qilin. The Kunpeng. These were encounters he had faced alone. No one—absolutely no one in this world—should know about the Three Great Sacred Beasts he interacted with.

"You think the Divine Eye of the Void is just a powerful tool?" You shook your head slowly. "It is a beacon. And the one who created it—the Heavenly Emperor—is not a myth, Zhuo Fan. He is not dead. He is watching."

The room temperature plummeted. Frost began to creep up the walls. Chu Qingcheng shivered, stepping back, looking between you and Zhuo Fan with confusion and fear. Yuan Xinggang looked pale, realizing this conversation had just ascended to a level beyond his Ethereal Stage understanding.

"The Heavenly Emperor is the enemy," you stated flatly. "And he is coming for his inheritance. You are cultivating his eyes, Zhuo Fan. Do you think he will let a thief keep them?"

You stopped a few paces from Zhuo Fan, crossing your arms.

"So, enough games. The High Venerable knows the future of the sect. I know the future of the cosmos. Now, will you stop pretending to be a talented disciple?"

You leaned in, your gaze drilling into his soul.

"Will you reveal who you really are, Zhuo Fan?"

The Reaction

Zhuo Fan stood frozen.

His mind was racing at a speed that would burn out a normal cultivator's brain. Heavenly Emperor? Alive?

To Zhuo Fan, the Ten Great Emperors of Antiquity were legends. They were dust in the wind of history. He knew of the Nine Serenities Emperor because he found the Nine Serenities Secret Records in his past life, which led to his death. But the idea that the Heavenly Emperor was currently alive—and hunting him for the Divine Eye art—was absurd.

And yet... you knew.

You knew about the Qilin. You knew about the Divine Eye of the Void. You knew things that even the Sacred Domain experts didn't know.

Slowly, terrifyingly, the "mask" of Zhuo Fan—the arrogant, talented youth from the Luo Clan—melted away.

His posture changed. He didn't grow taller, yet he seemed to tower over the room. His eyes, usually sharp and calculating, turned abyssal, filled with an ancient, weary arrogance. A thick, black mist began to seep from his skin.

"Hoh..."

A laugh escaped his lips. It was a cold, dry chuckle.

"Heavenly Emperor... active in this era? You tell a tall tale, 'Guest'."

Zhuo Fan’s right eye flashed. A purple golden lightning flickered within his pupil as he activated the first stage of the Divine Eye of the Void solely to test your reaction.

"But you know too much. You know of the Nine Serenities. You know of my cultivation. You speak as if you saw me in the Sacred Domain."

He stepped forward, the stone floor cracking beneath his foot. The killing intent he released was so potent it felt like a physical blade against your throat. He didn't believe the Heavenly Emperor was alive yet, but he definitely believed you were a threat to his secret identity.

"I am the Demonic Emperor, Zhuo Yifan," he declared, his voice echoing with the weight of a past life. "I don't know what nonsense you are spouting about ancient ghosts being alive, but since you know my true name... give me one reason why I shouldn't silence everyone in this room right now?"

He glanced briefly at Yuan Xinggang and Chu Qingcheng.

"Old Yuan... Qingcheng... close your eyes. This might get messy."

Zhuo Fan raised his hand, his fingers curling into a claw wreathed in black lightning. He was ready to kill to protect the secret of his reincarnation.

The Futile Strike

Zhuo Fan did not hesitate. The moment he decided you were a threat to his second life, he acted.

There was no shouting, no dramatic buildup. Just the ruthless efficiency of a Demonic Emperor.

Bzzt!

The purple lightning in his right pupil flashed. Divine Eye of the Void: First Stage—Shift.

In the blink of an eye, Zhuo Fan vanished from his spot and materialized instantly behind you. His hand, wreathed in the pitch-black energy of the Demon Transformation Art, clawed directly for your dantian. It was a strike meant to cripple your cultivation instantly, followed by a soul search.

"Too slow," Zhuo Fan whispered, his fingers inches from your spine.

Clink.

The sound of your teacup touching the saucer echoed through the room again.

Zhuo Fan’s hand stopped.

Not because he wanted to stop. But because he could not move forward. It wasn't a barrier. It wasn't spiritual pressure. It was simply... distance. No matter how hard he pushed, the inch between his claw and your back stretched into an infinity.

"Sit down, Little Demon," you said, without turning around.

A force that felt like the collapsing of a star pressed down on the entire room. It didn't crack the floor. It didn't shatter the walls. It bypassed the physical world entirely and weighed directly on the existence of everyone present.

Zhuo Fan was slammed back into his seat as if rewound by time itself. The black lightning on his hand sputtered and died. The Divine Eye in his right socket throbbed with excruciating pain, forcing him to shut it.

He gasped, clutching his chest, staring at your back with a look of genuine horror he hadn't felt since his death in the Sacred Domain.

The Witness of Antiquity

You slowly turned your chair to face him. You looked bored.

"You call yourself an Emperor," you said, your voice carrying the dust of aeons. "But you are just a child playing with broken toys."

You stood up and walked toward him. With every step, the shadows in the room seemed to twist, projecting images of a time long forgotten—massive beasts warring in the skies, mountains that touched the stars, and figures of light and darkness clashing.

"You think I 'know' these things because I read a scroll?" You scoffed. "Zhuo Yifan, knowledge is for those who study history. I am the history."

You leaned down, bringing your face level with his.

"I stood in the celestial court when the Heavenly Emperor first opened his eyes. I watched the Kunpeng soar before it was a terrified bird hiding in the mortal realm. I saw the Vaulting Kunpeng lose its eye. I saw the Soaring Qilin fall and its leg turn into the pillar of the heavens."

Zhuo Fan’s breathing hitched. "You... you are an Ancient Emperor? One of the Ten?"

"No," you corrected him gently, almost pityingly. "The Ten Emperors were powerful, yes. They ruled the era. But they were still players in the game. They fought, they bled, they died."

You straightened up, looking past the ceiling, past the sky.

"I was not one of them. I stood among them, but I was not of them. I was the silent guest at their banquets. I was the shadow in the corner when the Nine Serenities Emperor wrote his records. I am the one who watches the pieces fall off the board."

You looked back at him.

"And now, I am watching you, Zhuo Fan. You think you found the Divine Eye? You think you found the Nine Serenities Records by luck in your past life?"

You let that question hang in the air, heavy with implication.

"In the grand river of time, there are no accidents. The Heavenly Emperor isn't just 'alive', boy. He is the one who set the board. And right now, you are holding his favorite piece—that eye—and you think you are the player?"

You extended a hand toward him, offering him a choice again, but this time from a position of absolute superiority.

"I am the only one who knows how to flip the board. I am the only one who can help you survive the game you didn't even know you were playing. Now... tell me again who you want to kill."

The Memory of Water

Zhuo Fan remained silent, his chest heaving slightly as he processed the sheer scale of the entity standing before him. He was looking for a logical explanation, a loophole, something to ground himself.

You smiled, a cold, knowing smile that didn't reach your eyes.

"You are looking for the hand that moves the pieces, Zhuo Fan. Let me help you remember where you first felt its touch."

You took a slow sip of your tea, the liquid swirling like a vortex in the cup.

"Do you remember when you were in the Sacred Domain? Not as the Demonic Emperor, but before that. When you were just a little demon, a nameless cultivator struggling in the mud, barely scraping by—much like those four mischievous dwarfs of this sect."

Zhuo Fan’s brow furrowed. That was eons ago. A lifetime of blood and conquest had buried those memories deep.

He didn't teach you martial arts or cultivation techniques directly... he taught you how to see. Because of that foundation, you eventually had the capacity to understand the Nine Serenities Secret Records. Because of him, you became the Demonic Emperor."

Zhuo Fan’s eyes widened. The memory hit him like a physical blow. The dusty road. The humble tea shack. The man who spoke of the world as if it were a reflection in water.

You leaned forward, your shadow falling over him.

"You couldn't find him, Zhuo Fan, because he is the one who set the board."

The silence in the room was absolute. Even Yuan Xinggang stopped breathing.

Your rise, your fall, your death, and your rebirth... do you still think they were your own choices? Or were you just walking the path Water Mirror laid out for you?"

"A script," you finished for him. "A script to create the perfect vessel for the Divine Eye."

The Divine Move

Clack. You placed a white stone. Star point.

He created a complex web of deceit in the center of the board, a "Demonic Array" designed to swallow your territory whole.

He looked up, a faint smirk returning. "You see? The trap is set. If you move here, you lose the corner. If you move there, you lose the center."

You didn't even look at his trap. You picked up a white stone and placed it on a seemingly unrelated coordinate on the edge of the board.

Clack.

Zhuo Fan frowned. He looked at the board. Then he looked closer. His eyes widened.

That single stone... it didn't just ignore the trap. It rendered the trap irrelevant. By securing that specific liberty, his entire "dragon" in the center was now suffocating. His bait was not a bait; it was a corpse.

"You play very well, Zhuo Fan," you said, your tone devoid of mockery, stating it as a fact. "But you still have the tendency to rely on so many tricks. You play assuming your opponent has greed. You play assuming they will make a mistake."

You pointed to the dead dragon on the board.

"At the top, it is no longer about tricks. It is about playing the 100% accurate move. The Heavenly Dao does not get greedy. It just is."

You swept your hand over the board, dismantling his formation stone by stone as you spoke.

"Up there, the board is open and transparent like this chess board we are playing now. There are no shadows to hide in. The players are the other Ancient Emperors against the Heavenly Emperor and his sword—the Sword Emperor. All of them are wounded after their ancient war, which is why none have ever seen them since then. They are paralyzed in a stalemate of perfect moves."

Zhuo Fan felt a cold sweat breaking on his back. He realized he wasn't playing a game; he was being shown a map.

"One more piece of information," you said, placing a single white stone in the absolute center of the board—Tengen.

"This Mortal Domain... is actually a prison."

Zhuo Fan, Yuan Xinggang, and Chu Qingcheng all froze.

"A prison?" Yuan Xinggang gasped.

"Casted by the Heavenly Emperor with his Divine Eye of the Void," you continued, pressing your finger down on the stone. "He is intentionally pressing down all the cultivation of the creatures here. That is why the spiritual energy is so scarce. That is why no one has ever gone beyond the Genesis Stage here."

Zhuo Fan’s mind reeled. The cap on cultivation... the suppression he felt even in his previous life... it wasn't natural law? It was a shackle?

"Why?" Zhuo Fan whispered. "Why cage a world of ants?"

"Because the Sacred Beasts fled from him," you answered. "The Kunpeng, the Dragon, the Qilin... they hid in this dirt. So he cast a prison here to observe, waiting for the Sacred Beasts to come out so he could slaughter them."

You looked deeply into Zhuo Fan’s eyes—the eyes he stole from the Qilin, the art he learned from the Kunpeng.

"He isn't waiting for you, Zhuo Fan. He is waiting for the beast inside you to get fat enough to harvest."

You stood up, the game finished. Zhuo Fan’s territory was annihilated, not by force, but by a higher order of logic.

"The rest," you said, turning away, "you will hear from the Decimating Dragon Ancestor."

The Phantom’s Departure

You stood up from the Go board, dusting off your robes as if you had merely stopped by for a quick chat and not completely upended the fate of a world. The terrifying pressure that had suppressed the room vanished instantly, leaving the air light but charged with a new, heavy silence.

Zhuo Fan remained seated, staring at the single white stone on Tengen—the prison of the Mortal Domain. His mind was no longer racing with petty schemes against Xie Wuyue; it was expanding, recalibrating to a battlefield that spanned eons.

"Rewrite the script... break the board..." Zhuo Fan whispered.

His eyes slowly regained their focus, but this time, there was a desperate fire in them. He looked at you not as a threat, but as his only hope.

"Fine. You win. I am listening. What do you want me to do with Xie Wuyue? If we keep him as a puppet... how do we stop him from opening the gates?"

"Yuan Xinggang has lived through that timeline," you said, gesturing casually to the High Venerable. "He has seen the betrayal, the invasion, and the fall. Just hear him out, and you will know exactly where the rot is and how to cut it out."

You turned to look at Zhuo Fan one last time. The coldness in your eyes softened just a fraction—not into warmth, but into something resembling anticipation.

"Finally, after all this, you will not have just the Luo Alliance as your family. You will have the Demon Scheming Sect as well—cleaned from the rot, forged in fire. And trust me, Zhuo Fan... you will have many more family members later. The path of the Demonic Emperor is lonely, but the path of the True Self doesn't have to be."

Zhuo Fan looked up, startled by the mention of "family"—his one true weakness and his one true strength. Beside him, Chu Qingcheng’s eyes glimmered, sensing the implication.

"See ya," you waved, your voice fading like a distant echo. "We'll meet again."

The Aftermath

You took a step back, and the space around you folded. There was no flash of light, no tear in the void. You simply... ceased to be there. One moment you were a solid presence anchoring the room; the next, you were a memory.

The room was silent for a long time.

Clack.

Yuan Xinggang picked up a black stone and placed it on the board, right next to your white stone. It was a move of support, not attack.

"Zhuo Fan," Yuan Xinggang said, his voice steady and commanded by a newfound resolve. "We have work to do. Xie Wuyue will remain on the throne for now... but the strings are no longer in his hands."

Zhuo Fan took a deep breath, the purple lightning in his eye dimming as he returned to his calm, calculating self. But the arrogance was gone, replaced by the weight of a King who knows the sky is watching.

"Yes, High Venerable," Zhuo Fan replied, standing up and bowing—truly bowing—to the old man. "Tell me the future. We will rewrite it together."

The Demon Scheming Sect Arc is closed.

The seeds of the final battle against the Heavenly Emperor have been planted. Zhuo Fan is now aware of the prison, his Master Yuan is saved, and the board has been flipped.

Where shall we travel next?

**User:**
Anda berkata

Let's discuss about Naruto first without me being there but the theme is Naruto, Sasuke, and Kurama from Boruto the time reverted to when they are childrens. There are already many fan fictions about these where you may take ideas from them. Primarily, there are 2 versions where Naruto's parents passed away like in canon, and the other where they survived by splitting half of Kurama into Naruto and Kushina and Minato proceed throughout the series as hokage. Which version do you think is better?

---

**Gemini:**
This is a classic and beloved trope in the fandom—often called the "Peggy Sue" or "Time Travel Fix-It" genre. When you have Adult Naruto (Seventh Hokage), Adult Sasuke (Shadow Hokage), and a Cooperative Kurama thrust back into their 6-to-12-year-old bodies, you have a recipe for incredible storytelling.

You asked which version is better: The Canon-Divergence (Parents Alive) or the Canon-Compliant (Parents Dead).

Here is an analysis of both paths, followed by my recommendation on which one offers the deeper story.

Option A: The "Golden Timeline" (Parents Alive)

Minato and Kushina survived the Nine-Tails attack (perhaps Minato sealed half in Naruto and half in Kushina, surviving the reaper death seal). Naruto grows up as the Hokage's son.

The Appeal:

The "Imposter" Syndrome: This is a fascinating psychological angle. You have a 30+ year old Naruto who grew up an orphan, suddenly having to play "son" to parents he never knew. He would feel overwhelming love, but also awkwardness. He’s mentally older than his parents.

Political Thriller (Sasuke’s Arc): If Minato is alive, the Uchiha Massacre likely hasn't happened yet (or happened differently). Adult Sasuke has the chance to save his clan. Watching Adult Sasuke outmaneuver Danzo and debate philosophy with his father, Fugaku, while looking like a child is peak fiction.

The Ultimate Team-Up: Minato is a genius. If he figures out the truth (and he will), you get a "Team Minato + Team 7" alliance that destroys the plot.

The Downside:

Low Stakes: If Minato (Yellow Flash) is alive and you have two demigods (Naruto/Sasuke), the villains stand no chance. Orochimaru? Zabuza? The Akatsuki? They get steamrolled. The story becomes a "victory lap" with no tension.

Option B: The "Silent Guardians" (Parents Dead / Canon Start)

Naruto and Sasuke wake up in their messy apartments. Naruto is hated by the village. Sasuke is traumatized by the massacre. They are alone.

The Appeal:

Emotional Resilience: This version highlights how far they have come. Adult Naruto doesn't care if the villagers glare at him anymore; he waves at them. He treats the isolation with the patience of a Kage. It turns a tragedy into a display of strength.

The Secret Alliance: Since they have no parents watching them, Naruto and Sasuke have total freedom. They can sneak out at night, train in secret, and dismantle threats from the shadows. The image of two "children" sitting on the Hokage monument, discussing global politics while sharing a bento, is very strong.

Rewriting Tragedy: They have to look people in the eye who they know will die (The Third Hokage, Jiraiya, Neji). The emotional weight of saving them—or failing to—is much heavier here because they don't have Minato to hide behind.

Sasuke & Itachi: This is the strongest drama. Sasuke has to live through his "Avenger" phase again, but this time he knows the truth. Does he approach Itachi? Does he kill Danzo immediately? The tension of Sasuke acting like a brooding child while plotting a coup against the Elders is incredible.

The Verdict: Which is Better?

I believe Option B (Parents Dead / Canon Start) is the superior story.

Why?
Because Naruto is fundamentally a story about overcoming loneliness. If you give him his parents back immediately, you remove the core struggle that defines his character.

The most compelling narrative comes from Adult Naruto and Sasuke having to fix the world alone, from the shadows, while pretending to be incompetent genin.

Scene Concept: Imagine the Bell Test with Kakashi.

In Canon: They failed miserably.

In this Version: They have to pretend to struggle so Kakashi doesn't get suspicious, but their muscle memory is too good. They accidentally synchronize perfectly, terrifying Kakashi.

Kurama’s Role: In this version, Kurama is the only "parental" figure Naruto has left who knows the truth. Their banter becomes the emotional anchor of the story.

Suggested Plot Direction (For Option B)

If we proceed with Option B, here is a winning setup:

The Wake Up: They wake up the day of the Team Assignments. This skips the boring Academy days and jumps straight to the action.

The pact: Naruto and Sasuke meet at the training ground immediately. No words needed. They check their chakra reserves (tiny, pathetic). Kurama laughs at them.

The Goal: They agree to keep the timeline mostly intact to avoid the "Butterfly Effect" until they are strong enough to kill Black Zetsu.

The Divergence: They can't help themselves.

Zabuza/Haku Arc: Instead of a hard fight, Naruto talks Zabuza down with "Talk no Jutsu" (Hokage level charisma) or Sasuke speed-blitzes Gato. They save Haku and Zabuza, turning them into secret spies for Konoha.

Chunin Exams: They decide to humiliate Orochimaru not by fighting him (they are too weak physically), but by sealing his jutsu or setting a trap that makes him flee in terror, wondering "Who taught these brats Fuinjutsu?"

Would you like to start the simulation with Option B (Canon Start) on the day of the Team Assignments?

I see then all options are worth writing short stories. Make current option B -> option C. The new option B is Naruto parents passed away but the uchiha have not be annihilated. Option A and option B is where they are the youngest where their first goal is to prevent the annihilation of the Uchiha clan. **Gemini:**
This is a fantastic way to structure the scenarios. Organizing them by difficulty level—from the "Golden Route" (maximum resources, maximum happiness potential) to the "Hard Route" (minimum resources, maximum tragedy)—allows us to explore different facets of their characters.

Here are the three short story concepts, rearranged as you requested.

Option A: The Golden Route (The Solar Flare)

Status: Parents Alive, Uchiha Clan Alive.
Age: ~5 Years Old (Pre-Academy).
Difficulty: Very Easy (But Emotionally Heavy).

The Premise:
Naruto and Sasuke wake up in their 5-year-old bodies. Minato Namikaze is the Fourth Hokage and alive. Kushina is the terrifying but loving mother. The Uchiha Clan is prosperous, and Itachi is a happy older brother.

The Conflict:
The external threats (Obito/Madara/Danzo) are laughable against a team of Minato, Fugaku, Adult Naruto, and Adult Sasuke. The real conflict is internal. Naruto has to learn how to be a son after 30 years of being an orphan. Sasuke has to look at a father who is proud of him, without the baggage of the massacre.

The Strategy:

The Prodigies: They don't hide their skills. They exploit the "Child Prodigy" label to the max.

The Politics: Sasuke influences Fugaku to trust the Hokage. Naruto influences Minato to dismantle Danzo's Root early.

Story Snippet:

Naruto sat at the dinner table, staring at the bowl of rice. His hands—tiny, chubby, unscarred—trembled. Across from him, Minato was reading a scroll while eating, and Kushina was humming as she served more vegetables.

"Naruto?" Minato put the scroll down. "You haven't touched your food. feeling sick?"

"No," Naruto whispered, his voice cracking. In his mind, he was the Seventh Hokage, a man who had fought gods. But right now, looking at the blue eyes of the father he only met as a spirit, he felt like a toddler. "I'm just... happy."

Inside his seal, Kurama snorted. "Don't cry in your soup, brat. It's pathetic. Also, tell your dad his sealing formula on the toaster is sloppy. It's going to explode."

Meanwhile, at the Uchiha compound, Sasuke was staring at Itachi, who was poking his forehead.
"Forgive me, Sasuke, maybe next time," Itachi smiled.
Sasuke grabbed Itachi’s hand, shocking the teenager. "No next time," Sasuke said, his eyes possessing the intensity of a war veteran. "We train now. And watch out for Danzo. He wants your eyes."
Itachi blinked. "Sasuke?"

Option B: The Silver Route (The Twilight Pact)

Status: Parents Dead (Naruto is alone), Uchiha Clan Alive (Pre-Massacre).
Age: ~6-7 Years Old (Academy Entrance).
Difficulty: Hard (High Stakes, Time Limit).

The Premise:
This is the most tense timeline. Naruto is the pariah of the village, living alone. Sasuke is the happy prince of the Uchiha, but he knows the clock is ticking. The Uchiha Massacre is one year away.

The Conflict:
Sasuke cannot do this alone. He needs Naruto. But in this timeline, they aren't friends yet. Sasuke has to approach the "loser" Naruto and form a secret alliance to save his family. They have to stop Shisui's suicide and expose Danzo before Itachi snaps.

The Strategy:

The Secret Meeting: They meet at the Swing Set. No words needed, just a fist bump that checks for future memories.

The Intervention: They can't fight Danzo physically (too weak). They have to use Talk no Jutsu on Hiruzen and Tactical Intelligence to frame Danzo.

Saving Shisui: This is the turning point. If they save Shisui, the coup is stopped.

Story Snippet:

The sun was setting over the Academy. Naruto swung his legs back and forth, listening to the whispers of "Demon Brat" from the passing parents.

A shadow fell over him. He looked up to see Sasuke Uchiha. Not the brooding avenger, but a boy with a pristine shirt and a terrified look in his eyes that he was trying to hide.

"You're back too, aren't you?" Sasuke asked, his voice low.

Naruto stopped swinging. The goofball mask vanished, replaced by the weary gaze of the Seventh. "Yeah. Kurama's awake too."

Sasuke sat on the swing next to him, gripping the chains until his knuckles turned white. "Itachi is... he's acting strange. The clan meetings are getting louder. I have maybe six months, Naruto. Six months before my brother kills everyone."

Naruto jumped off the swing and dusted off his shorts. "Six months is plenty. We stopped Kaguya in a day. Stopping Danzo? Piece of cake. But first... we need to learn how to throw a shuriken again. My aim is terrible in this body."

"Speak for yourself," Kurama grumbled. "I still have plenty of chakra. Let's burn the Root HQ down tonight."

Option C: The Iron Route (The Shadow Legacy)

Status: Parents Dead, Uchiha Annihilated.
Age: ~12 Years Old (Team 7 Formation/Genin Exams).
Difficulty: Normal (Canon Start / New Game+).

The Premise:
The classic "Peggy Sue." The tragedy has already happened. Naruto is alone; Sasuke is the sole survivor. They wake up on the day of the Team Assignments.

The Conflict:
They are stuck in weak bodies with god-tier knowledge. The frustration is physical—they know how to do a Rasenshuriken or Amenotejikara, but their bodies break if they try. They have to act like incompetent Genin to avoid suspicion from Kakashi, while secretly preparing for the Chunin Exams invasion.

The Strategy:

Fixing Sakura: They decide early on to train Sakura properly so she doesn't lag behind.

Zabuza & Haku: They don't kill them. They recruit them as "Shadow Guards" for the Land of Waves.

Orochimaru: The goal is to terrify him. When Orochimaru bites Sasuke in the Forest of Death, Sasuke (with future mental fortitude) reverses the curse mark or traps a piece of Orochimaru's soul.

Story Snippet:

"Team 7," Iruka announced. "Naruto Uzumaki. Sakura Haruno. Sasuke Uchiha."

Naruto cheered (fake enthusiasm). Sasuke scowled (muscle memory). Sakura squealed.

Later, on the roof with Kakashi.

"My likes and dislikes?" Kakashi boredly asked. "I don't feel like telling you that."

Naruto and Sasuke exchanged a microscopic glance. They knew everything. They knew about Obito, Rin, the porn books, the mask, the depression.

"My dream," Naruto said, grinning. "Is to be a Hokage who actually does his paperwork."

Kakashi raised an eyebrow. "Oddly specific."

"My dream," Sasuke added, resting his chin on his hands. "Is to kill a certain man... and then maybe revive his clan using ethical science instead of revenge."

Kakashi stared. "What?"

"You two are terrible at acting," Kurama laughed in Naruto's head. "Just tell him you know he's Obito's friend so we can skip the bell test. I'm bored."

Which of these "Short Stories" would you like to develop further?
I personally find Option B (The Silver Route) to be the most compelling drama right now, as the "Countdown to the Massacre" provides a ticking clock that the other two lack.
