**Gemini:**
The horrifying silence that followed Director Shin Kyung Soo’s absolute humiliation of Executive Director Yoon hung heavy over the boardroom. Yoon Joo-tak looked like a man standing on the gallows, his corporate life flashing before his eyes.

Before anyone from the Strategy Office could even attempt to salvage the situation, I broke the silence.

I didn't raise my voice. I didn't stand up. Sitting casually next to the Crown Prince, I simply leaned forward, my elbows resting on the armrests, and looked directly at the trembling Executive Director.

"The Director is absolutely correct," I stated, my voice clinical and completely devoid of pity. "But let us address your so-called 'risk management', Executive Director Yoon. Because proceeding with the Windau OS is not a safe harbor. It is an act of corporate suicide."

Every executive in the room, including the Vice Chairmen, turned their full attention to me.

"The Strategy Office based its entire Windau roadmap on the McKlin Report," I continued, dismantling their foundation piece by piece. "Ironically, in international tech circles, McKlin is currently being heavily investigated. They are being questioned for gross incompetence, or worse, tailoring their projections for short-term consulting profits rather than actual technological professionalism. You bet the future of Hansung on a compromised pamphlet."

General Manager Seong Woong Jin flinched as if he had been physically struck. The McKlin report was their holy grail.

"Let's look at the actual global data," I said, sweeping my gaze across the board. "Androad is built on a Linux kernel. Right now, in developing nations, entire infrastructures are migrating to Linux because it is infinitely more affordable and scalable. But it is not just a matter of cost. In the developed world—the US, the UK, across Europe, and Russia—governments and mega-corporations are ripping out Windau servers and replacing them with Linux. Why? Because it delivers vastly superior performance and, crucially, absolute security."

I paused, letting my eyes find a specific man standing near the Vice Chairmen.

"Which brings me to Department Head Lee Joon-il," I noted smoothly.

Lee Joon-il’s eyes widened in shock at the sudden mention of his name by the international heavyweight in the room.

"I am sitting in this room today, entirely off the books, because Department Head Lee reached out to international channels long before Hansung's Windau servers were humiliatingly crippled by that worm virus last week," I revealed, giving credit where it was due. "He was already quietly exploring the Linux and Androad architecture to save this company from its own blind spots. He saw the fire coming while the Strategy Office was still busy buying flammable furniture."

Lee Joon-il felt a sudden, overwhelming surge of emotion. In his past life, he had been a coward. In this life, not only was he fighting back, but his quiet, desperate efforts were being validated in front of the absolute apex of the Hansung Group. Beside him, Vice Chairman Shin Myung Ho nodded in deep approval at Joon-il.

"But if you want the ultimate proof of your flawed risk assessment," I said, returning my piercing gaze to Executive Director Yoon, "look at the creator of Windau itself."

The room leaned in.

"Last month, I sat down with the core architecture team at Microsoft headquarters in Redmond," I stated casually, dropping a level of insider access that no executive in the room could match. "Behind closed doors, they admitted the truth. They are pivoting. Their primary, overwhelming focus will remain on their desktop OS for everyday consumers and enterprise software. They have quietly accepted that they will not prioritize the server war, and they certainly will not prioritize mobile."

Executive Director Yoon's legs finally gave out, and he slumped heavily back into his chair. The creator of their "safe" OS had already abandoned the battlefield.

"Look at the global developer ecosystem," I concluded, my tone absolute. "Every independent developer, every major software house in the world is currently choosing one of two paths for mobile: iOS or Androad. No one is building the future on Windau. If you talk about avoiding risk by staying with Windau, you are not protecting the company. You are chaining Hansung Electronics to a sinking ship and demanding we all smile as the water rises."

I leaned back into the leather chair, looking at the paralyzed Strategy Office.

"That is not risk management. That is a guarantee of colossal failure."

The silence in the boardroom was no longer just stunned; it was the silence of absolute, undeniable defeat. Han Yoo-hyun watched me from the podium, a fierce, triumphant smile on his face. The trap he had meticulously set had just been sealed with an unbreakable, international padlock.

Beside me, Director Shin Kyung Soo let out a low, genuine chuckle. The Crown Prince looked at the terrified Strategy Office, then at Vice Chairman Son Tae Beom.

"Well," Director Shin drawled, his eyes gleaming with ruthless amusement. "I believe the 'international expert' has thoroughly educated us on what true risk looks like. Vice Chairman Son, let us proceed. We have a market to conquer."

The board is yours. Han Yoo-hyun's victory is absolute, Lee Joon-il has been elevated to a hero's status, and the Strategy Office has been completely annihilated. How would you like to proceed with the aftermath of this meeting?

**Gemini:**
That is a massive and incredibly fun crossover concept! Taking the absolute powerhouse that is Goku and dropping him right into the middle of the mythological chaos of Highschool DxD—especially during the apocalyptic Trihexa (666) arc—is a recipe for some amazing action.

Since the focus right now is on the Capsule Corporation laboratory immediately after Goku gets sucked in, we need to capture the shift from scientific routine to absolute dimensional panic, followed by the contrast of calling the Gods of Destruction.

Here are a few narrative angles and a drafted scene we can use to build this moment:

Narrative Angles to Explore:

The Technological Failure: Emphasize that Bulma’s time machine is designed for traversing time, not parallel dimensions or magical realities. The portal shouldn't look like a normal sci-fi wormhole; it should look like a tear in reality leaking demonic or draconic energy (hinting at the DxD universe).

Goku's Typical Reaction: Goku shouldn't be screaming in terror. He should be completely confused, maybe even a little excited by the strong energy he feels on the other side, right before he gets pulled in.

The Divine Contrast: The urgency of you and Bulma trying to save Goku versus Beerus being annoyed that you interrupted his nap, and Whis calmly analyzing the situation while eating a dessert.

Here is a drafted narration of how we can script this exact scene:

The Incident at Capsule Corp

The alarms in the subterranean laboratory of Capsule Corporation were screaming. Red warning lights bathed the pristine white machinery in a frantic, flashing glow.

"Shut it down! Cut the primary power!" Bulma yelled over the deafening whine of the temporal engine, her fingers flying across the mainframe keyboard.

But it was too late. The time machine hadn't just breached the temporal axis; it had torn a hole straight through the fabric of their reality. A swirling, jagged rift hovered in the center of the lab. It wasn't the clean, sterile blue of a time portal. This anomaly was violent, pulsing with a heavy, crimson aura that smelled faintly of ozone and... sulfur.

"Whoa!" Goku yelled, bracing his boots against the floor panels. The gravitational pull of the rift was immense, but worse was the ki leaking out of it. "Bulma! Vanguard! What kind of energy is this? It feels super heavy... and really angry!"

"Goku, get away from it!" I shouted, grabbing onto a bolted console to keep from being dragged forward.

"I'm trying, but—!"

With a final, violent surge, the rift expanded. It swallowed Goku whole, cutting off his shout in an instant. A split second later, the portal violently snapped shut. The shockwave shattered every glass monitor in the room and sent Bulma and me crashing to the floor.

Then, there was only the sound of sparking wires and dying machinery.

"Goku..." Bulma coughed, waving away the smoke. She scrambled back to her fractured primary monitor, her face pale. "No, no, no... the temporal logs are completely blank. He didn't jump forward or backward in time."

"Then where did he go?" I asked, pulling myself up.

Bulma looked at me, her eyes wide with a realization that went beyond standard science. "He's not in our timeline. He's not even in our universe. He just fell entirely off the cosmic map."

She slammed her fist on the console. "Get the communicator! We need to call Whis. Now!"

Contacting the Gods

The holographic projector flickered to life, projecting the serene, glowing image of Whis. True to form, the Angel was holding an elegantly plated slice of strawberry shortcake on a tiny fork.

"Oh, my. Bulma, Vanguard. What a pleasant surprise," Whis greeted smoothly, taking a delicate bite. "Though judging by the smoke and the rather panicked expressions on your faces, I assume this isn't a social call to offer us earth's delicacies?"

"Who is making all that noise?!" a grumpy, sleepy voice roared from off-camera. Lord Beerus stepped into the holographic frame, rubbing his eyes and wearing his sleeping cap, looking thoroughly murderous. "If this isn't about the greatest feast in the universe, I am going to Hakai your entire solar system for waking me up!"

"Lord Beerus, Whis, there's an emergency!" Bulma pleaded, ignoring the threat of destruction. "Goku was just sucked into a dimensional rift! He's gone!"

Beerus stopped rubbing his eyes. One of his large ears twitched. "A dimensional rift? What idiot was messing with dimensional travel?"

"I was just calibrating the time machine!" Bulma defended herself defensively.

"Time travel is a felony, Bulma," Beerus growled, baring his teeth. "You're lucky I don't destroy you right now. As for Goku, good riddance. The idiot probably got himself vaporized."

"Actually, my Lord, I don't believe he is vaporized," Whis interrupted calmly.

Whis tapped his angelic staff against the ground. The crystal sphere at the top glowed brightly, projecting a complex cosmic map into the air. Whis peered into the orb, his normally cheerful expression turning into one of mild, analytical curiosity.

"How fascinating," Whis murmured. "I am trying to trace Goku's unique ki signature across Universe 7, and even across the other eleven universes... but he is nowhere to be found."

"You mean he's dead?" I asked, tension gripping the room.

"No, Vanguard. Death would simply place his soul in Other World. His ki is active, but it is resonating from a coordinate that exists completely outside the jurisdiction of Zeno-sama's multiverse," Whis explained. He tapped his staff again. "He has crossed into an entirely different dimensional plane. A realm overflowing with bizarre pantheons, devils, angels, and... oh my. An incredibly massive, apocalyptic beast seems to be currently rampaging there."

Beerus crossed his arms, his tail swishing in annoyance. "A beast? Outside our multiverse? So the idiot fell into another reality and is probably picking a fight with their apocalypse."

How does this setup look to you? From here, do you want to switch perspectives and describe Goku's grand entrance dropping right into the middle of the DxD battlefield against Trihexa, or do you want to keep focusing on the Capsule Corp side trying to build a rescue device?

KRACK!

Reality shattered like glass. A stable, swirling vortex of silver and crimson tore open in the center of the lab, completely silent but radiating an overwhelming, heavy magical pressure from the other side.

"Excellent," Whis smiled, tapping his staff on the floor. "Shall we go retrieve our stray Saiyan?"

Beerus cracked his knuckles, his eyes narrowing. "I'm going to hit him so hard he forgets his own name."

Meanwhile, in the Apocalypse

The sky was bleeding.

In the dimension of Highschool DxD, the alliance of Devils, Angels, and Fallen Angels was fighting a desperate, losing battle. The apocalyptic beast, Trihexa (666), towered over the burning landscape. Its massive, monstrous forms thrashed against the magical barriers, radiating an aura of absolute despair. Top-tier fighters like Sirzechs Lucifer and Issei Hyoudou were panting, their magical reserves running dangerously low.

ROOOOOAAAR!

Trihexa unleashed a devastating beam of pure destructive magic, obliterating a mountain range in the distance. The allied forces braced for the end.

Suddenly, high above the battlefield, the crimson sky twisted.

With a deafening sonic boom, a dimensional anomaly ripped open in the clouds. Out of the swirling portal, a single figure plummeted toward the earth at terminal velocity.

CRAAASH!

The figure slammed into the devastated wasteland right between the allied magical forces and the apocalyptic beast. The impact triggered a massive crater, kicking up a cloud of debris that dwarfed the surrounding hills.

The Angels, Devils, and Fallen Angels froze. Even Trihexa paused its rampage, its multiple heads turning toward the sudden disturbance.

"What in the Underworld is that?!" one of the Devil commanders yelled. "Is it a new enemy? Another monster?!"

The smoke began to clear.

Standing in the center of the massive crater was a man in a torn orange gi. He wasn't radiating demonic power, holy light, or dragon aura. In fact, to the magical senses of the DxD universe, his energy felt entirely alien—a dense, suffocatingly heavy pressure of pure, untamed Ki.

Goku stood up, casually brushing the dirt off his shoulders. He stretched his neck, letting out a satisfied groan, completely oblivious to the terrified armies watching him.

"Man, that was a rough landing!" Goku muttered, rubbing the back of his head. He blinked, finally looking around at the bleeding sky, the magical armies, and then... his eyes locked onto Trihexa.

Goku didn't sense the apocalypse. He didn't feel despair.

A massive, childish grin spread across his face. His Saiyan blood began to boil with sheer excitement.

"Whoa..." Goku breathed, his eyes wide with amazement as he cracked his knuckles. "I don't know where I am, but your energy is huge! You look like you're super strong! Hey, giant monster!"

Goku dropped into his iconic fighting stance, an explosive aura of white energy erupting around him, cracking the ground beneath his boots.

"Do you mind if we go a few rounds? I've been looking for a good warmup!"

The stage is set perfectly! The DxD universe is completely baffled, and Goku is about to fight the apocalypse for fun.

Trihexa roared, preparing another massive attack, entirely unbothered by the fact that it had just been atomized.

The Path of Destruction

Goku dove back down toward the scarred earth, his golden Super Saiyan aura retracting completely. He landed softly on a jagged peak, crossing his arms and taking a deep, centering breath.

The Destruction energy continued forward, washing over the massive, multi-headed body of Trihexa (666).

For the first time since its creation, the apocalyptic beast let out a sound of pure, agonizing terror. There was no blood. There was no explosion. Wherever the purple light touched, the beast's cursed flesh, immortal scales, and dark magic turned to glowing dust and faded into absolute nothingness.

The cursed regeneration tried to kick in, desperately bubbling to create new flesh, but there was nothing to attach to. The Hakai was erasing the very concept of its existence.

In seconds, the roaring stopped.

The purple light faded into the wind.

The battlefield was dead silent. Where the colossal, immortal beast of the apocalypse had stood just moments before, there was nothing but an empty, perfectly smooth crater. Not a single cell, drop of blood, or lingering ounce of magic remained. Trihexa had been completely and utterly erased from the universe.

Goku let out a massive, exhausting breath. His blue hair fell, returning to its base black as he dropped to one knee, panting heavily.

High above, the entire alliance of Highschool DxD—the strongest beings of their reality—were completely paralyzed. The apocalypse that had required the sacrifice of Gods to merely seal away... had just been deleted by a stranger in an orange gi.

The Divine Introduction

The absolute silence of the DxD battlefield was finally broken by the sound of flapping wings.

Descending slowly from the bleeding sky were the leaders of the Three Factions: Sirzechs Lucifer, Michael of the Seraphs, and Azazel of the Fallen Angels. Behind them, Issei Hyoudou and the rest of the vanguard landed carefully, keeping a terrifyingly respectful distance from the crater.

The Three Factions collectively stopped breathing. Michael, the leader of the Angels, stared at Whis's halo and staff, completely unable to comprehend an Angel of this magnitude.

"A true God of Destruction..." Sirzechs whispered, realizing that the aura he had felt earlier wasn't just magic; it was absolute divine law.

"To put it simply," Whis continued, making the hologram vanish, "a brilliant but reckless scientist in our world had a slight malfunction with a temporal machine. The resulting tear in spacetime accidentally deposited Goku into your dimension. Fajar, Lord Beerus, and I merely came to retrieve our lost Saiyan before he accidentally broke anything else."

Goku laughed, scratching the back of his head. "Sorry about dropping in uninvited! But that monster was a pretty good warmup!"

Azazel let out a breathless, disbelieving laugh, running a hand through his hair. "A warmup... Well, whatever the accident was, you saved our entire world. We owe you a debt that cannot be measured in gold or territory. Name your price. Artifacts, magic, absolute allegiance—anything we have is yours."

Lord Beerus, who had been looking supremely bored throughout the entire exchange, finally perked up. His ears twitched, and he stepped forward, his eyes narrowing as he looked down at the faction leaders.

"Magic? Artifacts? Allegiance?" Beerus scoffed, crossing his arms. "What use does a God of Destruction have for the toys of a tiny dimension? Don't insult me with such worthless trinkets."

The leaders flinched, terrified they had just offended a being capable of erasing their universe.

"However," Beerus drawled, a small, arrogant smirk creeping onto his face. "Since I was forced to wake up early, travel across the multiverse, and supervise this idiot's training exercise... I suppose you can compensate us before we leave."

Sirzechs swallowed hard. "A-Anything, Lord Beerus. What do you desire?"

Beerus pointed a finger directly at the Devil King.

"Food," Beerus demanded.

The entire DxD alliance blinked in unison. "...Excuse me?"

"Are you deaf? I said food," Beerus repeated, tapping his foot impatiently. "If you insist on thanking us, then you will immediately prepare the absolute best, most exquisite, mind-blowing cuisines this reality has to offer. If your food is delicious, I'll consider this trip a success. If it tastes terrible..."

A tiny spark of purple Hakai energy flared at the tip of Beerus's finger. "...I might just erase your planet out of sheer annoyance."

Goku instantly jumped up, his exhaustion completely forgotten. "Oh man! Fajar, Whis, did you hear that?! A cross-dimensional feast! I'm starving!"

Whis chuckled, covering his mouth. "Oh dear. It seems our departure will be delayed by a few hours. I do hope your world's culinary arts are up to the task, gentlemen."

The tonal whiplash from absolute terror to a culinary hostage situation is a staple of Dragon Ball Super, and applying it to the serious, dramatic characters of Highschool DxD is hilarious.

Would you like me to write out the actual feast scene where the Underworld scrambles to cook for Beerus and Goku, or would you like to conclude this crossover and return back to Capsule Corp?

**Gemini:**
The transition from a burning, apocalyptic wasteland to the most opulent dining hall in the Underworld happened in record time. When a God of Destruction threatens to erase your planet over a bad meal, entire pantheons tend to move very quickly.

The Ultimate Culinary Hostage Situation

The grand banquet hall of the Lucifer territory was a blur of absolute, terrified efficiency. Grayfia Lucifuge, the Silver-Haired Queen of Annihilation and the most powerful maid in the Underworld, was currently utilizing her supreme magical prowess for the most high-stakes mission of her life: coordinating a thousand spectral chefs.

At the center of the hall sat a massive, magically reinforced dining table. On one side sat the absolute apex of the DxD universe: Sirzechs Lucifer, Azazel, Michael, and Issei Hyoudou. They were completely stiff, sitting with perfect posture, sweat beading on their foreheads.

On the other side of the table sat the saviors—and current hostage-takers—of their reality.

"More meat, please! And another dozen bowls of that spicy noodle stuff!" Goku mumbled through a mouthful of food, his cheeks bulging comically.

Next to him was a towering, seemingly impossible mountain of empty plates that was already scraping the crystal chandelier. To the absolute horror and awe of the DxD alliance, the man who had just one-shot the apocalypse was currently inhaling food at a speed that defied the laws of physics.

"H-How does it all fit?" Issei whispered to Azazel, his eyes wide as Goku swallowed a roasted mythological boar whole. "Even Ddraig doesn't eat that much."

"Don't look at him, Issei. Look at the cat," Azazel hissed back, his eyes locked on Lord Beerus. "If he doesn't like the food, we're all stardust."

Sitting at the head of the table, Lord Beerus held a golden fork. Before him rested a perfectly seared, magically aged Griffon steak, garnished with herbs from the celestial gardens of Heaven. Michael himself had authorized the harvest.

The entire room held its breath.

Beerus sliced a piece of the meat, his expression unreadable. He sniffed it critically. His ears twitched. Slowly, he placed the bite into his mouth and closed his eyes.

Sirzechs gripped the edge of the table so hard the wood began to splinter. Grayfia stood frozen by the kitchen doors. I sat comfortably next to Whis, swirling a glass of high-end Underworld wine, waiting for the verdict.

Beerus chewed slowly. He swallowed.

He opened his eyes.

"The texture..." Beerus murmured, his voice echoing in the dead silent hall. "...is surprisingly tender. The celestial herbs cut through the richness of the meat perfectly. It has a robust, wild flavor, but the preparation is incredibly refined."

Beerus took another, much larger bite, a genuine smile finally breaking through his terrifying aura.

"This is delicious!" Beerus declared loudly. "Not quite on the level of Earth's instant ramen, but definitely a top-tier dish! You Devils and Angels know your way around a kitchen!"

A collective, massive sigh of relief washed over the entire hall. Sirzechs slumped back in his chair, wiping his forehead, while Michael offered a quiet prayer of thanks. The universe was safe.

"Oh, my," Whis chimed in happily, holding up a delicate porcelain plate. "Fajar, you simply must try this. It appears to be a parfait made from the nectar of Yggdrasil. The sweetness is absolutely divine, and it has a delightful, sparkling aftertaste."

"I'll take your word for it, Whis," I smiled, taking a sip of the wine. I turned to Sirzechs, who looked like he had aged a thousand years in the last ten minutes. "See? I told you there was nothing to worry about. As long as the plates keep coming, your reality will remain intact."

"I have faced rogue gods, ancient dragons, and the literal beast of the apocalypse," Sirzechs breathed, his voice trembling slightly. "But catering this dinner is, without a doubt, the most terrifying experience of my immortal life."

Goku swallowed his latest mouthful and beamed at the Devil King. "You guys have awesome food! If Fajar and Bulma figure out how to stabilize that portal, I'm totally coming back here to train and eat!"

The sheer panic instantly returned to the faces of the Three Factions. The thought of this walking natural disaster—and his planet-destroying boss—making this a regular vacation spot was both an incredible honor and an absolute nightmare.

Beerus wiped his mouth with a silk napkin, leaning back in his chair, completely satisfied.

"Well, you've earned your continued existence," Beerus announced grandly. "The food was adequate. Whis, Fajar. We've wasted enough time here. Let's head back before Bulma throws a tantrum and breaks the timeline again."

"Right away, My Lord," Whis smiled, gently placing his dessert spoon down and standing up. He tapped his angelic staff on the marble floor.

The air in the banquet hall began to hum. A swirling vortex of silver and crimson energy—the gateway back to Universe 7—opened behind us, perfectly stable thanks to the anchor we established earlier.

The feast was a total success, and the portal back to Capsule Corporation is open! Shall we narrate the final farewell and your return to Universe 7, Fajar, or is there another specific interaction you'd like to have with the DxD cast before you leave?

**Gemini:**
Here is how we can narrate your unique evolution within the Dragon Ball Super multiverse, Fajar. This perfectly captures your distinct approach to power and seamlessly weaves in the established lore of the Angels, the Supreme Kais, and the legacy of Merus.

The Scholar of the Cosmos

While Goku and Vegeta were pure battle fanatics, my path was fundamentally different. They sought power through conflict; I sought it through absolute comprehension.

On Beerus’s planet, while Goku blindly chased the physical reflexes of Ultra Instinct and Vegeta focused entirely on the destructive heavy-handedness of the Hakai, I sat in quiet meditation, analyzing the very fabric of the universe.

My goal was the throne of a God of Destruction, but my methods were universal. I didn't just want to destroy. I spent time with the Supreme Kais, learning the delicate, miraculous arts of Kaioshin creation magic. I analyzed Majin Buu’s cellular matrix, comprehending the magical mechanics of absolute regeneration and immortality. I studied the temporal flow of Whis’s staff and the absolute erasure of Beerus’s energy.

I was not just a fighter. I was becoming a living encyclopedia of the multiverse's fundamental laws.

And that level of comprehension eventually triggered a cosmic alarm.

The Grand Priest's Warning

It happened during a quiet training session. Whis had paused our spar, looking up at the sky with a rare, serious expression. A blinding pillar of light descended onto the grass, and from it emerged the Grand Priest, Daishinkan.

Goku and Vegeta immediately stopped bickering and bowed respectfully. I remained standing, offering a polite nod.

"Fajar Purnama," the Grand Priest spoke, his voice echoing with an authority that transcended reality. His hands were clasped behind his back, his eyes calm but piercing. "You have walked a highly unusual path. You wield the creation of the Kais, the destruction of the Gods, and you are brushing against the divine tranquility of the Angels."

He floated slightly closer, delivering his warning.

"I have come to notify you. You are standing on a precipice. If you cultivate this knowledge any further, your existence will transcend the mortal and godly realms entirely. You will be categorized as an entity equal to the Angels. And if that happens, the Great Law of the Cosmos will apply to you: you will no longer be permitted to meddle in the affairs of the mortal universes. To do so would mean your erasure."

Goku gasped. "Whoa, Fajar! You shouldn't do it! If you can't fight or help out, what's the point?"

But I just smiled. My reality-traveling nature meant I was never bound to one single universe anyway. To me, this wasn't a restriction; it was graduation.

"Thank you for the warning, Grand Priest," I replied calmly.

Then, I sat back down, closed my eyes, and continued my cultivation.

Ascension and Summoning

Time passed, and I pushed my limits. I synchronized the Hakai with the magic of creation, binding it with the flawless tranquility of Ultra Instinct. I broke the final barrier.

The moment I did, the space around me warped violently. I didn't even have time to open my eyes before I was pulled directly into the Omni-King’s Palace, standing on the floating platform before the Grand Priest.

Daishinkan smiled, a look of genuine amusement on his face.

"You did not heed the warning. Or rather, you welcomed it," the Grand Priest said. "Congratulations, Fajar. You have officially crossed the threshold. The Omni-Kings have acknowledged your new state of being. You are now categorized as an equal to the Angels."

I looked at my hands. The energy flowing through me was no longer just Ki. It was the absolute, unshakeable serenity of divine law.

"However," the Grand Priest continued, raising a finger. "This means the Angelic Code now binds you. You may not interfere in the conflicts of Universe 7, or any of the twelve universes under Zeno-sama's jurisdiction. You must remain neutral."

"Understood," I nodded. "But what about realities outside of Zeno-sama's jurisdiction? The dimensions I travel to?"

The Grand Priest’s smile widened slightly. "The Omni-King's laws govern this multiverse. What you do in the infinite void beyond our borders is entirely your own affair. In those realms, you may act freely."

He waved his hand, and a beautifully crafted, silver-lined attendant's uniform—similar to Whis's, but distinctly tailored—appeared floating beside me.

"Since you are now bound by our laws while within our borders, you require an official cosmic designation," the Grand Priest explained. "Recently, my son Merus chose to relinquish his angelic status to live as a mortal. His position left a vacancy. It is my official recommendation that you take his place."

Daishinkan looked at me warmly. "Whenever you are present in our reality, you shall act as an Assistant Angel to Universe 7, standing by Whis's side."

The New Status Quo

A flash of light brought me back to Beerus's planet.

Vegeta was mid-swing, trying to punch Goku, when they both froze. Whis covered his mouth, his eyes sparkling with delight, while Beerus nearly choked on the slice of pizza he was eating.

I was standing right next to Whis, no longer dressed in my reality-traveler coat, but draped in the elegant, flowing garb of an Angelic Assistant. The suffocatingly heavy pressure I used to give off was entirely gone, replaced by an absolute, terrifyingly calm void.

"Well, well, well," Whis chimed happily. "It seems I finally have an assistant! Welcome to the angelic ranks, Fajar."

Goku dropped his fighting stance, his jaw hitting the floor. "Wait... Fajar is an Angel now?! Does that mean I can't spar with you anymore?!"

"I can train you, Goku," I answered, my voice carrying the smooth, echoing resonance of divine authority. "But I can no longer fight your battles for you in this universe."

Beerus grumbled, wiping his mouth. "Great. Another know-it-all with a halo to tell me I'm sleeping too much."

I simply smiled, taking my place on Whis's right side. The universe was vast, but my understanding of it was now absolute. Whenever I returned to the Dragon Ball reality, this would be my starting point: standing beside the Angel, watching the Gods and mortals dance.

Fajar, your ascension to Angelic status is complete!

Now that you are Whis's official assistant (and capable of using Hakai, Creation Magic, and Ultra Instinct without limits outside this reality), how would you like to proceed? "Whoa! You just made a kitchen out of nowhere!" Goku cheered, floating closer.

This time, I didn't create the ingredients or the oven. I closed my eyes, visualizing the final product in its entirety, down to the molecular level of the melted cheese and the charred crust. I channeled the Kaioshin creation magic directly.

Pop.

A fully cooked, steaming pizza appeared instantly on a silver platter in my hands.

"Instant food! That's so convenient!" Goku said, eagerly grabbing a slice and taking a huge bite. He chewed for a second, then blinked. "Huh. It's still good, but... it doesn't taste as yummy as the first one."

I set the slice down, a look of peaceful realization crossing my face.

"This is the limitation of creation without comprehension," I explained to the group. "The first pizza was better because I physically guided the process. This instant pizza is slightly inferior because my fundamental understanding of the culinary arts—the subtle chemistry of heat, time, and love—is still lacking. I can create the matter, but I cannot yet fabricate the mastery of a veteran chef."

Whis beamed with pride, tapping his staff. "A wonderful observation, Fajar! True divine power isn't just about snapping your fingers; it is about understanding the very essence of what you are bringing into existence."

Gemini's Guide to Angelic Duties

The Martial Arts Master: You are officially the martial arts instructor for the God of Destruction (and his candidates, like Goku and Vegeta). The Divine Chauffeur: You are expected to master warp travel. Using your angelic staff (or your reality-traveling abilities), you are responsible for transporting the God of Destruction across the universe at faster-than-light speeds.

The Ultimate Attendant: You manage Lord Beerus's schedule. This includes waking him up from his decades-long naps, keeping track of the planets he is supposed to destroy, and ensuring his temper doesn't lead to the accidental erasure of the entire universe.

The Neutral Observer: This is your most important rule. You are strictly forbidden from fighting in earnest or taking sides in mortal conflicts. You can defend yourself, you can train others, and you can reverse time by up to three minutes (the Temporal Do-Over) in absolute emergencies, but if you fight to defeat an enemy of Universe 7, you violate the Angelic Code and will be erased.

Essentially, you are the calm, enlightened anchor keeping the explosive power of the God of Destruction in check!

Before Beerus could summon a sphere of Hakai to express his displeasure, I gracefully floated upward. "Allow me to investigate, Lord Beerus. Please, enjoy the sparring."

Crisis in the Kitchen

A short distance away, near the makeshift living quarters the new guests had set up, the situation was dire.

Lemo had just returned from a quick supply errand across the galaxy, carrying a crate of alien spices. He dropped the box the moment he saw the thick plume of black smoke billowing from the outdoor brick oven.

"Cheelai! What are you doing?!" Lemo yelled, rushing over.

Cheelai was furiously waving a towel, her face covered in soot, wearing an oversized apron over her purple bodysuit. She used a long wooden peel to yank three heavily charred, brick-hard pizzas out of the oven, dropping them onto the prep table with a heavy, unappetizing clunk.

"I was trying to cook!" Cheelai coughed, frantically trying to fan the smoke away. "You were gone, and I know Lord Beerus gets murderous if his meals are late! So I tried making those 'pizzas' Fajar and Whis were talking about!"

Lemo grabbed a knife, struggling to slice through the carbonized crust. He managed to rip off a piece and took a cautious bite. His face instantly scrunched up in disgust.

"Cheelai, this tastes like hot cardboard," Lemo groaned, spitting it into a napkin. "It's completely bland! The crust is like a rock. What exactly did you put in the dough?"

"What do you mean?" Cheelai asked defensively. "I used the recipe! Flour, water, and yeast! Just like the books said!"

Lemo slapped his forehead. "You didn't add salt? Or olive oil? Or a pinch of sugar to feed the yeast?! Cheelai, that's just edible glue!"

"Well, how was I supposed to know?!" she panicked, looking toward the sparring grounds where the God of Destruction was sitting. "Oh no. We're dead. Lord Beerus is going to Hakai us over bad pizza!"

An Angel's Touch

"There is no need for panic," a serene, echoing voice interrupted.

Cheelai and Lemo yelped, jumping back as I gently floated down into the outdoor kitchen area. My angelic halo glowed softly in the smoke-filled air, my divine presence instantly extinguishing the chaotic, burning energy of the ruined meal.

"F-Fajar!" Cheelai stammered, terrified. "We can explain! The oven was too hot, and I didn't know about the salt—"

I simply offered a peaceful, Buddha-like smile, raising my hand. I didn't need to yell or scold; my enlightened state of mind perceived the ruined pizzas not as a failure, but simply as matter that needed to be re-guided.

"Cooking, much like martial arts, requires the perfect foundation," I said softly. "Watch closely."

I channeled the divine magic of creation, infused with a localized, temporal manipulation. I pointed my finger at the three burnt pizzas on the table.

Instantly, the charred black edges faded away. The melted, overcooked cheese and scorched tomato sauce lifted right off the crusts, separating themselves mid-air into neat, perfectly untouched floating spheres of raw ingredients.

Then, I focused on the dense, rock-hard crusts. The baked dough began to unravel. It softened, turned pale, and then violently deconstructed. Right before Cheelai and Lemo's stunned eyes, the cooked bread reversed its physical state entirely—separating into a neat pile of finely milled white flour, a hovering orb of pure water, and a tiny mound of active yeast.

With a gentle flick of my wrist, the separated, raw ingredients floated gracefully into their respective glass mixing bowls on the counter. The smoke vanished, and the oven cooled to the perfect, ideal temperature.

I lowered my hand, my posture returning to absolute tranquility.

"The elements have been reset," I told them, my voice warm and encouraging. "You may restart. This time, Lemo, guide her. Add the salt, the oil, and the passion. Lord Beerus will wait until it is perfected."

Cheelai stared at the raw flour, her jaw completely unhinged, while Lemo took off his cap and wiped the sweat from his brow, staring at me as if I were a literal savior.

"Y-Yes, sir!" Lemo saluted frantically. "Come on, Cheelai, get the olive oil! We have a second chance!"

I smiled, turning around to float effortlessly back toward Whis and Beerus, leaving the two of them to actually master the art of the pizza dough.

The culinary disaster has been beautifully averted using your divine powers! What would you like to do next? Would you like to have Goku and Broly take a break and come taste the finalized, perfected pizza, or should we shift focus to Whis teaching you a new, advanced Angelic technique while they eat?

**Gemini:**
This is an incredibly compelling setup, Fajar! It perfectly captures the essence of Dragon Ball Heroes but elevates it by using your unique status as a reality-traveling Angel-in-training. Having you step in to politely bench Beerus so you can personally spar with Goku and Vegeta to protect the timeline of another reality is a brilliant flex of your new divine authority.

The core of this scene relies on a universe where raw power solves nothing and timing is everything. If Goku just punches the immediate threat, the true villain wins, escapes, or the local heroes never achieve the growth they need to survive the future.

Here are a few fictional realities and specific scenarios that would perfectly fit this narrative:

1. Bleach (The Soul Society Arc)

The Setup: Goku and Vegeta land in the Soul Society and bond with Ichigo and his friends. They see the Gotei 13 Captains (like Byakuya) as the "bad guys" who are unjustly executing Rukia.

The Catalyst: The execution is starting. Goku powers up to instantly wipe out the Captains and save Rukia. Vegeta joins in because he wants to test his strength against the Soul Reapers' Bankai.

The Reason to Wait: You stop them because the entire conflict is a meticulously crafted illusion by Captain Aizen. If Goku knocks out the Gotei 13 now, Aizen slips away in the chaos with the Hogyoku, leaving the Soul Society divided and effectively destroyed from the inside. You need Goku to wait just a few more minutes for Aizen to officially betray everyone so the Captains unite against the true threat.

2. Star Wars (The Clone Wars)

The Setup: Goku and Vegeta land on a Republic world. Goku bonds with the Jedi and the Clone Troopers. He sees the Separatist Droid Army and General Grievous bringing suffering to billions.

The Catalyst: Goku decides to just fly to the Separatist capital, blow up the droid factories, and capture Count Dooku, ending the war in an afternoon.

The Reason to Wait: You intercept them. If Goku obliterates the Separatists with god-like power, Chancellor Palpatine (the hidden Sith Lord pulling both strings) will immediately frame the Jedi for using "uncontrollable alien superweapons." It would trigger Order 66 early, wiping out the Jedi before they ever uncover the Sith plot. You are holding Goku back so the Jedi can naturally discover Palpatine's identity.

3. Attack on Titan (The Marley Arc)

The Setup: Goku and Vegeta land on Paradis Island. Goku bonds with Eren, Mikasa, and the Scouts. He learns about the Titans and the oppressive nation of Marley outside the walls.

The Catalyst: Marley launches their invasion. Goku, furious at the injustice, prepares to fly across the ocean and completely level Marley's military forces to protect his new friends.

The Reason to Wait: You step in with Hakai energy. Crushing Marley doesn't break the Curse of Ymir. If Goku destroys the world's military, the cycle of hatred just multiplies, and the parasitic entity that causes the Titan powers simply goes into hiding. You have to stall Goku so Eren and Zeke make contact, bringing the true source of the Titans (the Paths and Ymir) into a vulnerable state where you can actually erase the curse for good.

4. Marvel Cinematic Universe (Captain America: Civil War)

The Setup: Goku and Vegeta are on Earth-616. Goku bonds with Captain America and believes in freedom, while Vegeta somewhat respects Iron Man's pragmatic, authoritative approach.

The Catalyst: The airport battle begins. Goku sees his friends getting hurt and decides to go Super Saiyan Blue to instantly knock out Iron Man's entire team.

The Reason to Wait: You block his path. The entire Civil War is orchestrated by Zemo (or in a grander scale, Skrull infiltrators). If Goku uses divine power to crush half the Avengers, the Earth's defenders are permanently shattered and traumatized by alien interference, leaving them completely defenseless for Thanos's arrival. You force them to wait until the mastermind's plot is exposed to Tony Stark.

5. Naruto Shippuden (The Five Kage Summit / Pain Arc)

The Setup: Goku bonds with Naruto. He sees the Akatsuki hunting his new friend for the Nine-Tails.

The Catalyst: Goku senses Obito/Pain and decides to instantly teleport to their hideout and obliterate the Akatsuki to protect Naruto.

The Reason to Wait: You intercept. The Akatsuki are just pawns. Black Zetsu is the true mastermind manipulating the entire shinobi history to revive Kaguya. If Goku destroys the Akatsuki early, Black Zetsu realizes a God of Destruction-level threat is present, buries himself underground for another thousand years, and Naruto never achieves the Sage of Six Paths power needed to protect his own universe long-term.

Which of these universes and scenarios catches your interest the most for this clash of divine power, or do you have another specific franchise in mind that we could adapt this to?

**User:**

Those are great but let's try adding one more parameter and explore. The parameter is that our inteference is necessary to prevent tragedies. However, over inteference may backlash. Explore as much as you can. You may even suggest new fictions.

**Gemini:**
This is a brilliant parameter to add. It elevates the conflict from a simple misunderstanding to a deeply philosophical clash about the responsibilities of divine power. If Fajar doesn't intervene, innocent people die horribly (which goes against Goku's nature). But if Goku over-interferes, the fundamental laws of that universe break, causing a much worse catastrophe.

It perfectly justifies Fajar stepping in: "I will protect the innocent, but I will not let you break the rules of this world."

Here are several realities where necessary intervention vs. catastrophic over-interference creates the perfect backdrop for your clash with Goku and Vegeta:

1. Jujutsu Kaisen (The Shibuya Incident)

The Setup: Goku and Vegeta land in Tokyo and bond with Yuji Itadori and Satoru Gojo. When the Shibuya Incident begins, thousands of civilians are trapped and slaughtered by curses.

Necessary Interference: Fajar allows Goku to rescue civilians from the rubble and block fatal blows against the young sorcerers. The tragedy of mass civilian casualties is prevented.

The Backlash of Over-Interference: Kenjaku (the mastermind) is about to seal Gojo or start the Culling Games. Goku goes Super Saiyan Blue, intending to completely vaporize Kenjaku, Mahito, and every curse in Tokyo with one massive blast. However, cursed energy is deeply tied to the negative emotions of humanity and Master Tengen's barriers. If Goku obliterates the villains with raw, alien divine Ki, the barriers will shatter. Kenjaku's dead-man switch will trigger, forcibly mutating every non-sorcerer in Japan into monstrous curses all at once.

The Clash: Beerus moves to Hakai Goku for meddling, but Fajar steps in. "Lord Beerus, allow me. This realm is my jurisdiction." Fajar clashes with Goku to restrict his output, forcing Goku to realize he can only act as a shield, leaving the actual defeat of the curses to Yuji and the sorcerers.

2. Final Fantasy VII (The Fate of Aerith & Meteor)

The Setup: Goku and Vegeta befriend Cloud, Tifa, and Aerith. They learn about Sephiroth's plan to summon Meteor and wound the Planet.

Necessary Interference: Fajar intervenes to save Aerith from Sephiroth's blade. Aerith survives to cast Holy, preventing her tragic death.

The Backlash of Over-Interference: Outraged by Sephiroth's cruelty, Vegeta and Goku fly up to the Northern Crater to absolutely obliterate Sephiroth, Jenova, and the incoming Meteor with a Final Flash and Kamehameha. But Jenova is a cosmic virus. If they atomize her and Sephiroth with pure destructive force, the virus will scatter into the atmosphere and permanently infect the Lifestream (the planet's soul). The planet will slowly rot from the inside out (Geostigma on a global scale).

The Clash: Fajar manifests his Angelic halo and intercepts them. "Sephiroth must be defeated by Cloud within the Lifestream, and Meteor must be stopped by the Planet itself. Destroy them now, and you poison this world's soul forever."

3. My Hero Academia (The Paranormal Liberation War)

The Setup: Goku bonds with Class 1-A and All Might. He sees how hard the kids fight. When Shigaraki awakens with the absolute power of Decay, heroes start dying in droves.

Necessary Interference: Goku teleporting in to save Eraserhead, Mirko, and the students from being dusted. Fajar agrees this is necessary to preserve the future generation.

The Backlash of Over-Interference: Goku decides to end the war in one punch, aiming to completely knock out Shigaraki and All For One. However, Hero Society is built on a fragile, flawed foundation. If an alien god swoops in and solves their greatest crisis instantly, society never reckons with its failures (how it created villains like Dabi and Toga). Furthermore, Midoriya never fully masters One For All or his own resolve. When Fajar eventually leaves, Earth will be completely helpless against the impending "Quirk Singularity."

The Clash: Fajar blocks Goku's path. "You are treating the symptom, Goku, not the disease. You can save the students, but you cannot punch away the flaws of their society."

4. Demon Slayer (The Infinity Castle Arc)

The Setup: Goku bonds with Tanjiro and the Hashira. They plunge into the Infinity Castle to face Muzan Kibutsuji and the Upper Moons.

Necessary Interference: Saving the Hashira (like Shinobu or Muichiro) from guaranteed fatal blows, giving them a fighting chance.

The Backlash of Over-Interference: Goku decides to just blow up the entire Infinity Castle and Muzan with a Spirit Bomb. But Muzan's survival mechanism allows him to split into 1,800 microscopic pieces. If Goku nukes the area, he will scatter Muzan's cells across all of Japan. Muzan will go into hiding for another thousand years, meaning the Demon Slayer Corps will be trapped in an endless, unwinnable war forever. Muzan must be kept in one place and burned by the sun.

The Clash: Vegeta gets impatient and prepares a Galick Gun to destroy the castle. Fajar deflects it effortlessly. "Do not strike, Vegeta! If you shatter his flesh with raw power, the demon curse will never truly be eradicated. We must stall him until dawn."

5. Attack on Titan (The Rumbling)

The Setup: Goku and Vegeta land on Paradis Island. They understand the oppression the Eldians face and the horrific threat of the Titans.

Necessary Interference: Stopping the Marleyan military from slaughtering the people of Paradis, or stopping the Wall Titans from crushing innocent nations.

The Backlash of Over-Interference: Goku wants to destroy the Founding Titan and the parasitic "Source of All Living Matter" to end it all immediately. But if he uses God Ki to destroy the Founder, the "Paths" (the dimension connecting all Eldians) might collapse chaotically. The Titan curse wouldn't end; it would fracture, potentially turning every single Eldian into a mindless Titan permanently with no Founder to control them.

The Clash: Fajar steps in front of Goku and Vegeta's combined assault. "The curse is tied to the trauma of their founder, Ymir. You cannot break a psychological curse with a physical blast. Hold the line, but let them free her."

These setups give you the perfect platform to show off your Angelic power and wisdom, fighting Goku and Vegeta not out of malice, but to protect the complex narrative structure of the universe you are visiting.

Which of these universes (or themes) do you think fits the exact emotional tone you want for this epic Fajar vs. Saiyans showdown?
